Trans-Pacific Flight Attempt by Japanese Aviator 75

Departed from Tokyo Yesterday Morning

Reuter's Tokyo, 10th - The Japanese third attempt to fly across the Pacific Ocean is now in preparation for completion. This time it is initiated by Hochi Shimbun, the navigator is Kiyoshi Honma, the pilot is Eiichiro Baba, and they will probably bring a radio operator. They plan to depart from the beach of Rin-dai. The aircraft is a Junkers long-range monoplane, equipped with a special engine. The first stop is planned at Nome, Alaska; the second stop is Fairbanks, Alaska; the third stop is Hazelton, Canada; and then they will fly along the coast to Seattle. However, the aviator hopes to fly directly to the mainland United States after landing in Nome, only flying over Fairbanks. According to Hochi Shimbun, they initiated a trans-Pacific flight once this year, planning to fly from the United States to Japan, but it was stopped after destroying two aircraft during test flights.

Reuter's Tokyo, 10th - The Hochi Shimbun airplane departed from Tokyo's Haneda airfield at 11:07 this morning, planning to stop briefly at Rin-dai in northern Japan, and then head east. In the autumn of last year, Pangborn and Herndon successfully completed the non-stop flight across the Pacific Ocean, also using Rin-dai as their departure point.

New York Ferry Steamer Explosion 76

Ninety-Seven Dead and Injured

Havas, New York, 9th - An unfortunate incident occurred today on the East River crossing New York. The New York City government-hired "Observation" ship was carrying more than two hundred workers to Rikers Island to build a prison. En route, the steam boiler suddenly exploded. The cause of the accident is still unknown. Thirty-seven bodies have been found. Most of the survivors were injured, thirteen of them severely. According to witnesses, they suddenly saw thick smoke rising. After the smoke cleared, the ship disappeared, and only those who escaped were seen floating on the water, struggling against death. United Press, New York, 9th - According to the latest investigation of the ferry accident, a total of thirty-nine people died, fifty-eight were injured, and several are missing. The cause of the ship's explosion is currently being investigated in three separate investigations. Most of the rescued people pointed to the malfunction of the boiler, which was installed about twenty-four years ago. The government police and the ironworkers' union are now each starting their own investigations.

Page 13

Important News

Wang Shengrong and Others Report the Truth of Two Attacks on Shenyang 77

Burning More Than Seventy Japanese Aircraft

Beiping Correspondence: At the end of last month, the leaders of the righteous army, Wang Shengrong and Zhao Shulin, twice attacked Shenyang, shocking China and Japan. However, many of the reports in China proper still do not match the facts. A special letter was sent from Beiping to report the truth of the attack on Shenyang. It is recorded as follows:

(Omitted above) Before attacking Shenyang, the righteous army leaders Sheng Yu, Wang Dawei, Rong Zhaohua, Zhao Dianliang, etc. discussed the plan to attack Shenyang all day long. Finally, it was decided to start the attack after Mutō arrived in Shenyang, and it was agreed to act together at 10:00 p.m. on August 28. That night, Wang Dawei led more than two thousand righteous soldiers to take charge of the south side, Sheng Yu led more than one thousand righteous soldiers (including the broadsword team) to take charge of the west side, and Rong Zhaohua led six hundred people to take charge of the northeast side. At around 10:00, the south route sneaked in through the South Gate, the west route sneaked in through [omission], and the northeast route sneaked in through the Feng-Hu Station of the Great North Gate. At this time, the enemy's military police had not yet noticed. It happened that a certain Japanese consultant was riding in a yellow car to Feng-Hai Station, and met our army advancing on the northeast route. Our army suspected that the Japanese had noticed and were coming to attack. Our army immediately opened fire, (at this time it was not yet 10:00) immediately killing the three Japanese people in the same car, and continued to advance. At this time, the southwest routes heard the gunfire and rushed in from all directions. After a fierce battle between the northeast route and the Japanese puppet military police, in addition to killing and wounding more than 20 policemen, more than 10 Japanese people were killed (including several Japanese military officers), and more than 130 enemy military police guns were seized. Then they surrounded the radio station and destroyed its important parts. Finally, they attacked the Japanese station. After a fierce battle between the south route and the Japanese military police, more than 20 police guns were seized, and more than 10 Japanese soldiers and officers were killed and wounded. The weapons, clothing, hats, and command knives of the wounded and killed Japanese officers were also seized. Later, they joined other routes to the two major aircraft factories and burned all the aircraft (mostly old ones, about 70). After the burning, they also concentrated on the Japanese station for a general attack. At this time, on the west route, Sheng Yu, Zhao Dianliang, Li Juchuan, Lin Zisheng, etc. were carrying out guerrilla warfare against the Japanese station to contain the Japanese reinforcements, so that they would not dare to go elsewhere, and waited for all routes to arrive together to occupy the Japanese station in one fell swoop. However, at this time, the artillery fire from the Japanese station was very dense, and fires started everywhere. Our army was afraid that innocent civilians would be affected, so they retreated immediately. After the retreat, they rested for one day on the 29th. At 11:00 p.m. on the 30th, they attacked according to the original plan. When the struggle began, the Japanese were terrified, and the Japanese station was in a deadly hail of bullets. This night's hard battle is difficult to describe in detail. If there had been sufficient ammunition, machine guns, and heavy artillery, Shenyang could definitely have been captured. At the same time, Liaoyang, Fushun, Xinmin, Kaiyuan, and Dashiqiao could all respond. Then, how difficult would it be to recover the lost territory of the Northeast? It is hoped that our compatriots, gentlemen, and patriots will give considerable assistance. This would be the good fortune of the righteous army and the good fortune of the country. The Shenyang Righteous and Brave Army, Wang Shengrong and Zhao Shulin, along with thousands of strong soldiers, jointly announce (September 8).

Suppression Army's General Offensive on XInji and Honghu 78

Hankou Correspondence: Recently, the military affairs of suppressing bandits have focused on eastern Hubei and central Hubei. The central and left routes have advanced simultaneously, with Xinji and Honghu as their destinations. Since the general offensive of the central route troops on the 15th of last month, they have successively captured Huang'an, Qiliping, Tuanshugang, and Bopihe, with irresistible force. The remaining bandits took Xinji as their refuge, and fled to that place one after another, building fortifications and attempting to resist stubbornly. The various armies then advanced on separate routes, and the air force assisted in bombing. The most bombs were dropped in Xinji and the Yuanqiang River to the north, Hujia Chong and Fan Jia River to the northeast, and the Huwan and Wangjiawan areas southwest of Bopihe, and the most bandits were killed. All of the bandits' grain platforms, fortresses, and power lines were destroyed. On the 8th, Commander Zhang Fang reported by telegram that the Red bandits were extremely panicked at the active offensive of our army. The only bandits who could fight were the pseudo-Red Fourth Army and the Twenty-fifth Army, claiming to be eighteen regiments, resisting east and west, but fleeing after a single battle, or using flags to confuse our army. According to Commander Chen Jicheng's telegram, according to the reports of the captured and escaped soldiers, many of the houses in Xinji were destroyed by our aircraft bombing, and the order was extremely chaotic. The pseudo-important institutions have been moved to other places, leaving only a small number of personnel and the pseudo-headquarters to command the bandits. The bandit area is lacking in food and bullets. Each bandit has at most one hundred bullets, or as few as ten or dozens of bullets. Their predicament can be imagined. Zhang Fang, Wei Li, and Chen Jicheng are all on the front line, and have set a deadline to recover the bandit nest in Xinji. It is heard that the bandits have a plan to abandon Xinji and flee back to their old nest in Jinjiazhai, on the border of Anhui. According to Liu Gangfu, the director of the 14th Army's resident office in Hankou, after Wei Junzhang Lihuang recovered Qiliping and Tuanshu, he led two tracking teams to pursue and attack, fighting fiercely on one side to prevent bandits from crossing, and on the other side to prevent the input of grain and weapons, and then using a large army to suppress them. Division Commander Zhang Zhenhan and others all went to the front line in person. He Chenjun, the commander of the left-wing army, and Xu Yuanquan, the deputy commander, also often went to the front line by plane to give instructions. In the past ten days, XIngouju and Zhoulaoju were recovered in one battle, and Qujiawan and Liujiaji were occupied in another. The bandit's barriers have gradually become owned by the national army. On the 8th, the national army also recovered Zhuhe, as well as Daishi and Yufengkou in Hubei. Only two mounds in Quanhu are still in the hands of the bandits. The lake has been blockaded for a long time, and food and rice are lacking. Many coerced bandits took the opportunity to surrender, and the total number has reached thousands. Those who are still in the bandit area, as soon as they see airplanes distributing leaflets, rush to pick them up to see if there are any words of coercion and non-treatment. The national army, because most of them are coerced people, cannot bear to kill them all. Personnel trained by the army divisions use propaganda methods to persuade them to return. It is heard that the Red bandits are not very afraid of the national army's attacks, but they are most afraid of using political power to disperse their masses. Therefore, there is a metaphor that leaflets are more powerful than artillery shells. Winning hearts is the most important thing in suppressing bandits today. Regarding the recent combat situation, Xu Yuanquan had a very detailed telegram on the 7th, which is recorded as follows: "After our army captured XIngouju, Yanglinguan, Zhouliuju, and cleared the surrounding remnants of bandits, we used the 41st and 48th Divisions to attack Fenyang, Liujiaji, Pijiatan, and Xiaoshakou, the bandit dens in various places, at the same time on the 7th at dawn, The bandits had defensive works in various places, which were unusually strong, and the dikes were broken in front of them, with widths of several feet, connecting the lake water. Fortunately, the officers and soldiers bravely waded and swam, regardless of their own safety, and finally defeated the bandits in various places on that day, killing more than 300 bandits on the spot, capturing more than 200 guns, and seizing a radio. A group of remnant bandits fled to Zhuhe, and the rest fled into the lake in small boats. After detailed search for several days, it was found that four pseudo-military hospitals, one general hospital of the Xiang-E-West Province, and one arsenal were searched in Eryudun, Erchouhe, Zhoujiawan, Nanheshi, and Dukou. Most of them were newly built buildings with complete equipment and large capacity. Except for the medical staff who escaped from the hospital, more than 3,000 wounded bandits were abandoned. Except for the important parts that had been moved into the lake from the arsenal, each piece of electrical equipment and a large net bed for manufacturing rifles were searched. The rest of the pseudo-institutions included the Provincial Military Commission, the General Labor Union, the Mutual Aid Association, the Second Branch of the Military Academy, the Management Office, the Ordnance Bureau, schools, libraries, clubs, stadiums, telephone networks, printing houses, etc., which have all been evacuated. Except for documents and articles that have been ordered to be collected and inspected, the abandoned houses and bulky items have been burned to avoid being left for bandit use. Five hundred hostages from Tianqian, Mianying, Jinghan, and Chuan were found in the prisons in various places, and they have all been released and given money to return to their hometowns. Now that the bandit area has been recovered, the aftermath is being dealt with, and the troops are prepared to continue to clear the bandit dens in the lake in order to completely eradicate and fundamentally eliminate them. I send this telegram, Xu Yuanquan Yangxi Xingshen Yin" (September 9).

Han Fuqu's Statement on the Zhang Case 79

The Provincial Party Department Asks the Central Government to Pardon Zheng Jicheng

Jinan Correspondence: Zheng Jicheng, who assassinated Zhang Zongchang, is currently being held in the military court. According to the statement of Han Fuqu, the chairman of the provincial government, regarding this case, the provincial government has received many documents from the families of the victims in recent days, all requesting the provincial government to forward them to the central government for a pardon for Zheng Jicheng. However, the provincial government feels that it has no authority to deal with this matter. Director Zhang of Beiping sent a letter to me, asking about the course of the case, and I have already replied. Mr. Wan (Fulin) also sent a telegram (stating that this case was unexpected and a pity, etc., and the statement of returning to legal resolution must be shown by a telegram from the central government, and the provincial government can hand over this case to the court for handling only if Zhang's family sues. Now the central government has only replied with a "understood" to the provincial government's report telegram, and Zhang's family has not sued, so as of today, Zhang Jicheng has not been sent to the court, and is still being detained in the military court. My personal feeling is that if a central figure comes to Jinan, the local government should have the responsibility to guarantee him. However, Zhang Zongchang was originally a civilian, and since he came to Jinan, the local government wanted to [omission], but it was difficult to [omission] the name, etc. Zhang Lucun, the standing committee member of the Provincial Party Department, also made a statement, stating that the party departments in various places have been sending telegrams like snowflakes in recent days, and the representatives of the families who were brutally harmed by Zhang Zongchang have also sent documents to the Provincial Party Department, all requesting a pardon for Zheng Jicheng. The issue was brought up for discussion at today's routine meeting of the Provincial Party Department, and the resolution was roughly as follows: "After investigation, the deceased Zhang Zongchang was a traitor who sold out the country and harmed the people during his lifetime, and harmed comrades of this party. He should have been punished by the law of the country long ago. However, he could not be arrested, which caused him to be punished for a long time. This time, Zheng Jicheng assassinated him, which is no different from acting on behalf of the law of the country. The people are happy. We should send a telegram to the central government to forward to the national government to issue a clear order to pardon Zheng Jicheng for no crime, and trace the crimes of the traitor Zhang, and announce it to China and foreign countries to uphold justice and discipline." It is also heard that the Provincial Party Department will compile documents from all parties and forward them to the central government together. During the two years of the Republic of China, many people were killed by Zhang, since Du Shanmin, the wife of Du Huayu, and others initiated the joint petition of the families of the victims and the victims of the May 3rd Incident to support Zheng, many people have joined. The families of the victims will have a large-scale movement to support Zheng, and request the provincial government and the Party Department to forward the request to the central government in order to pardon Zheng. (9th)

Recent Situation of Banditry in Jiaodong 80

Qingdao Correspondence: Since the beginning of autumn in the Jiaodong area, the green gauze tent has risen, and banditry has become rampant. Kidnappings and robberies are heard every day, and even arson and massacres have turned villages into ruins. The tragic situation is unbearable to witness. The banditry in various counties is briefly recorded as follows:

Zhucheng: Youjiguan Village, fifty miles away from the city in the western township of the county, was suddenly attacked by more than 200 bandits from Ju County at about 8:00 p.m. on the 2nd of this month, with complete firearms. They sneaked in from the northwest corner and attacked the village. The village originally had a militia for defense, but because the incident was sudden, it was cut off by the bandits. Some retreated to the southeast corner of the village, and those who did not have time to retreat defended themselves with the house walls and fought against the bandits. The bandits searched and killed at will, and many farmers who could not hide were brutally harmed. The bandit leader, angered by the militia's resistance, ordered arson. For a time, the fire shone into the sky, visible from more than ten miles away. The sound of gunfire was as dense as a string of pearls, and the villagers cried out in misery, reaching for several miles. The Zhigou militia, ten miles away from the village, rushed to help after hearing the alarm, but was also defeated by the bandits due to their small numbers. At 4:00 p.m. the next day, the garrison in the city rushed to the rescue and opened fire with the bandits three miles away from the village. The fierce battle shifted for a while, but it was still ineffective. Fortunately, more than 30 Zhigou militiamen arrived to help in the battle, attacking from both sides. At 6:00 p.m., they counterattacked into the village and finally repelled the bandits who had been entrenched in the village for a day and a night. After the incident, the investigation revealed that more than 80 villagers were killed or injured, mostly elderly, women, and children who could not escape. The strong men who died were the militiamen who resisted the bandits with guns. More than 200 houses were burned, and property losses amounted to more than 30,000 yuan, which is a tragic disaster that Zhucheng has never seen before.

Rizhao: The county's mountains are rugged and have always been a place where bandits come and go. At the end of last month, more than 200 bandits suddenly came to the vicinity of Yougushan in the southwest township of the county. That night, they moved to Suoluoshu Village. The villagers fled in panic upon hearing the news. Those who could not escape were captured by the bandits. The bandits occupied the village for three days, and all the grain, grass, property, cattle, donkeys, chickens, and ducks were looted. Doors, windows, and sundries were all broken with axes to cook rice. The crops in the fields were also mostly eaten and trampled clean by the bandits' mules and horses. When leaving, they also took away more than 40 male and female hostages, passing through Shuichegou and Hezhuang to Zhulou. Shangyuan and Nanjiezhuang were also burned by the bandits one after another. The villages were already very poor, but now they have suddenly suffered this catastrophe, which is truly lamentable. As for the case of kidnapping, it is everywhere in the county, so the villagers are startled several times a night and dare not stay in peace.

Gaomi: A large number of bandits were also found near the border between Gaomi and Changi recently, kidnapping everywhere. Rong Guangxing, the brigade commander of the 87th Brigade stationed in Jiaoxian, sent Battalion Commander Jin to lead a battalion of soldiers to Gaomi to supervise the suppression. They chased to a village in Changi County and encountered the bandits. The two sides opened fire and fought fiercely for several hours, killing 47 bandits on the spot, capturing 14 alive, rescuing more than 20 hostages, and obtaining a dozen guns. More than a dozen soldiers were also injured. It is heard that after Brigade Commander Rong slightly interrogated the bandits, he sent troops to escort them to Jinan for punishment according to law. (September 7)

Legislative Yuan Revises the Law on Handling Labor-Capital Disputes 81

The Central Political and Legal Conference previously proposed by Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of Shanghai, to amend the Law on Handling Labor-Capital Disputes and restore compulsory arbitration, or to allow Shanghai to formulate separate laws and regulations and adopt compulsory arbitration (Wu's original proposal was published in this newspaper on August 8). It was decided to restore the compulsory arbitration method and submit it to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. The 196th meeting of the Legislative Yuan decided to submit it to the Labor Law Drafting Committee for review. The 199th meeting then presented a report which, after deliberation, was submitted to the Labor Law Drafting Committee to be reviewed jointly with the Economic Committee and the Military Committee. After receiving the order, the committee held a joint meeting on September 2 and sent letters to various ministries, including the Ministry of Military Affairs, the Ministry of Political Affairs, the Ministry of Industry, the Ministry of Communications, and the Ministry of Railways, as well as the Construction Committee, the Nanjing Municipal Government, and the Shanghai Municipal Government, requesting each to send representatives to attend the meeting and state their opinions. It was decided to amend the texts of Articles 4, 15, 16, 20, and 44, and also to amend Article 23 of the Trade Union Law, which has an additive relationship with compulsory arbitration. It was submitted to the 201st General Assembly of the Legislative Yuan on September 10 and passed with amendments. The amended version is recorded as follows:

Amended Law on Handling Labor-Capital Disputes Chapter 1 General Provisions (Article 1) This law applies when a dispute arises between an employer and a labor group, or 15 or more workers, regarding the maintenance or change of labor conditions. (Article 2) The administrative authority responsible for this law, unless otherwise specified, is the municipal government in the city and the county government in the county. The competent authority for a special industry is its administrative office. (Article 3) When a labor-capital dispute occurs, the administrative authority should convene a mediation committee to mediate upon the request of one or both parties to the dispute. If the administrative authority believes that there is a need for mediation, it should do the same even without the request of the parties. When mediation is successful, it is regarded as a contract between the parties to the dispute. If one of the parties is a trade union, it is regarded as a collective agreement between the parties. (Article 4) For labor-capital disputes in the following industries, if the matter is mediated without results, it should be submitted to the arbitration committee for arbitration: (1) Water, electricity, or gas industries for public needs; (2) Postal, telegraph, telephone, railway, tramway, shipping, and public automobile industries for public use. (Article 5) For labor-capital disputes other than those in the previous article, if mediation fails, it should be submitted to the arbitration committee for arbitration upon the request of both parties to the dispute. However, if the administrative authority believes that the dispute is of great importance and has lasted for more than one month without resolution, and deems it necessary to submit it to arbitration, it may submit the dispute to the arbitration committee for arbitration even without the request of the parties. (Article 6) Labor-capital disputes may not be submitted to arbitration without mediation procedures, unless both parties to the dispute request direct arbitration. (Article 7) The parties to the dispute may not appeal the decision of the arbitration committee. The decision in the preceding paragraph is regarded as a contract between the parties to the dispute. If one of the parties is a trade union, it is regarded as a collective agreement between the parties.

Chapter 2 Agencies for Handling Labor-Capital Disputes Section 1 Mediation Agency (Article 8) Mediation of labor-capital disputes is handled by the mediation committee. (Article 9) The mediation committee consists of five or seven members, organized by the following representatives: (1) One or three representatives appointed by the administrative authority; (2) Two representatives appointed by each party to the dispute. The representatives in the first item of the preceding paragraph are not limited to the staff of the administrative authority. (Article 10) When a labor-capital dispute should be submitted to mediation in accordance with the provisions of Article 3, paragraph 1, the parties to the dispute should each select or appoint a representative and report the representative's name and address within three days after receiving the notice from the administrative authority. The administrative authority may extend the time limit in the preceding paragraph as appropriate when it deems necessary. If the representative's name and address are not reported within the time limit, the administrative authority may designate them ex officio. (Article 11) After the selection of members of the mediation committee is determined, the administrative authority should convene a meeting as soon as possible, and the representative appointed by the administrative authority should serve as the chairman. However, the mediation committee stipulated in Article 13, paragraph 3, should have a representative appointed by the Ministry of Industry as the chairman. If the mediation committee has convened a meeting, but the members refuse to attend, causing the mediation to fail, it is deemed that the mediation has failed. (Article 12) The chairman of the mediation committee may transfer staff from the administrative authority or the local court in the area to handle records, filing, drafting, and all other general affairs. (Article 13) If there are two or more administrative authorities in charge of the same labor-capital dispute, and each administrative authority is in the same province, the administrative authority in the first item of paragraph 1 of Article 9 is designated by the provincial government. When necessary, the representatives in the first item of paragraph 1 of Article 9 may also be designated by the provincial government. If the same labor-capital dispute is not in the same province, the administrative authority in the first item of paragraph 1 of Article 9 is designated by the Ministry of Industry. If the Ministry of Industry deems it necessary, the representatives in the first item of paragraph 1 of Article 9 may be designated by the ministry. In the preceding two cases, for state-owned enterprises, the designation or appointment is made by its competent authority. Section 2 Arbitration Agency (Article 14) Arbitration of labor-capital disputes is handled by the arbitration committee. (Article 15) The arbitration committee consists of five members, organized by the following personnel: (1) One representative appointed by the administrative authority; (2) One representative appointed by the provincial party headquarters or the local municipal or county party headquarters; (3) One representative appointed by the local court; (4) One representative each from the labor and capital sides who have no direct stake in the dispute. (Article 16) Every two years, the provincial government or the municipal government not under the province should order labor groups and employer groups within its jurisdiction to nominate 24 to 48 persons who are qualified to be arbitration committee members, list their names, and submit them for approval and then report them to the Ministry of Industry for record. Every two years, the Ministry of Industry should order labor groups in state-owned enterprises and separately order the direct administrative organs of each enterprise to nominate 24 to 48 persons who are qualified to be arbitration committee members, list their names, and submit them for record. In the event of an arbitration, the representatives in the fourth item of the preceding article should be designated by the administrative authority from the lists in the preceding two items who have no direct stake in the dispute. The methods for nominating arbitration committee members in the first and second items are determined by the Ministry of Industry. (Article 17) Anyone who has served as a member of the mediation committee may not be a member of the arbitration committee for the same event. (Article 18) The arbitration committee is convened by the administrative authority, and the representative of the convening agency serves as the chairman. However, the arbitration committee stipulated in Article 20 should have a representative appointed by the Ministry of Industry as the chairman. (Article 19) The chairman of the arbitration committee may transfer staff from its affiliated agency or the local court in the area to handle records, filing, drafting, and all other general affairs. (Article 20) For the same labor-capital dispute, if its scope is not limited to one province, except for state-owned enterprises, the representatives in the first item of Article 15 are designated by the Ministry of Industry, and the representatives in the fourth item are designated by the Ministry of Industry from the list of arbitration committee members in the relevant provinces. (To be continued)

Hangzhou Airplane Crash Account 82

Hangzhou Dispatch: At 9:40 AM on the 9th, the Aviation School of the Military and Political Affairs Department in Jianqiao, Hangzhou, dispatched two training planes, numbers 8 and 5, for two instructors to practice formation flying. Instructor Shi Manniu was in plane number 8, along with Chen Shenfu, the eldest son of the martyr Chen Yingshi (recommended by Chairman Chiang to the school for a make-up exam before enrollment). Instructor Zhang Guodong piloted plane number 5, accompanied by Kang Taihong, a technician from the school. They circled the city for forty minutes before returning to the airfield. Upon returning, the upper and lower wings of the two planes collided, and they crashed simultaneously. Plane number 8 was completely shattered. Instructor Shi Manniu's brains were splattered, and his back was broken. Chen Shenfu had a swelling of three or four inches on his left forehead, a high purple swelling on his chest, and his right arm and left leg were both fractured with skin still attached. His body was riddled with fragments from the shattered plane, and he died instantly. Plane number 5 only suffered damage to its wings and tail, with the fuselage remaining intact. Zhang and Kang suffered minor injuries. The details are as follows:

Cause of the Accident: Aviation instructor Zhang Guodong is recuperating at Guangji Hospital due to injuries. Zhang is from Jing County, Hebei Province, and is 39 years old. Zhang has been an instructor since the aviation school was first established. According to Zhang, the aviation school has not yet officially opened, so the instructors practice on their own daily. Yesterday, Instructor Shi took Chen Shenfu in plane number 8, and I took Mr.

Kang in plane number 5. At that time, we were practicing formation flying. My plane was on the upper left, and Shi's plane was on the lower right. When returning to the airfield, plane number 8 was jolted by an air current and suddenly rushed up towards plane number 5. There was a loud explosion, and Shi's plane crashed straight down. Although the wing of plane number 5 was damaged and the engine was also broken, fortunately, with the help of the wind, it descended slowly, and I was spared from death. I only suffered minor injuries to my left finger, right arm, and waist, with slight skin abrasions. Technician Kang also suffered skin injuries in several places.

Shi and Chen's Demise: Instructor Shi Manniu was 32 years old, from Jingzhou, Hubei Province, and had served in the aviation field for a long time. During the Northern Expedition, he repeatedly performed meritorious deeds in the Battle of Longtan. His wife is also in her thirties and has three children: the eldest is eight years old, named Xinman, and is already studying at Qiushi English School; the second is four years old, and the youngest is only two years old. Mrs. Shi is currently eight months pregnant. Shi's body was placed in a coffin last night and temporarily moved to the Caishen Temple in Jianqiao this morning (the 10th). It is reported that Shi also has an elderly mother in her sixties, and an elder brother named Zifeng, who works on the Longhai Railway, both currently in Zhengzhou, Henan. Shi's wife has already telegraphed her brother to report the tragic news of Shi's death. Chen Shenfu was 20 years old, his mother is still alive, and he has a younger brother named Zuhe. Chen graduated from the high school department of Zhijiang University this summer and applied to the aviation school a few days ago. He happened to be ill, and then received a telegram from Chairman Chiang on the 6th to retake the exam. Principal Mao did not allow him to fly for training because he had not undergone a physical examination. The day before yesterday, Instructor Shi was practicing flying, and Chen, being acquainted with Shi, insisted on flying with him. Shi agreed, but unexpectedly, this led to his death. After Chen Shenfu's death, the aviation school immediately telegraphed Chairman Chiang, Chen Guofu, Chen Lifu, and Chen Quanshi, Chen's uncle from his ancestral home of Wuxing. Quanshi received the news and rushed to Hangzhou that night. The Guofu brothers came to Hangzhou with Yingshi's wife at 1:45 PM on the 10th. After arriving at the station, they went to Zhu Mingtao's residence in Kui Lane with Mao Bangchu and others to discuss the funeral arrangements for his younger brother. Then, they went to Jianqiao together. In the evening, they placed his younger brother in a coffin so that he could be transported back to his hometown for burial. Aviation School Memorial Service: Aviation School Principal Mao Bangchu said that the airplane accident yesterday is viewed as shocking by outsiders, but in the aviation world, it is very common. Since the success of the airplane in 1903, accidents, both direct and indirect, in the aviation industry of advanced countries have been good materials for our research. Moreover, our country is just beginning to engage in the aviation industry, so we should not be discouraged by this accident. Rather, we should use the accident to gain more experience. The aviation industry of the world today has sacrificed countless lives. Mao also said that at 9:30 AM on the 10th, the aviation school had already held a simple ceremony to mourn Shi and Chen. Once the school's facilities and layout are in order, a grand memorial service will be held. (10th)

A Journey to the West (19) 83

Trembling with Fear at the Nose of Yama

On the morning of the 25th, our army was about to leave Luochuan, and everyone felt uneasy in their hearts, as if a great disaster was about to befall them. Having previewed the itinerary, we knew that we would soon encounter the "Nose of Yama," the Jiudaoshou Mountain (mountain name). The difficulty of the road was evident from its name. At that time, the group leader, Mr. Hu, was also quite worried about the unusual dangers of this trip. When he inquired about the possibility of bypassing the mountain, the locals replied with "Leopard Head Slope." In fact, the "Nose of Yama" was the name used by porters, while "Leopard Head Slope" was the name used by the local people. Although the names were different, they referred to the same place. When we heard Mr. Hu's report that we could bypass the "Nose of Yama" during breakfast at 6:30 AM, we were all overjoyed. At 7:00 AM, everything was ready, and we set off. I and Mr. Ou and five others rode ahead. At first, the road was flat and easy to travel, and we did not feel any hardship. An hour later, the so-called "Nose of Yama, Jiudaoshou Mountain" arrived. At first, the mountain road sloped downwards, almost like a vertical wall, appearing and reappearing in an endless series of switchbacks, causing the riders to tremble with fear. After one mountain had been crossed, and a small stream forded, there was an even larger mountain blocking the way ahead. We urged our horses straight upwards, and the higher we climbed, the less steep the slope became. Before we reached the mountainside, all five horses were already panting heavily. Looking up at the summit, we heard voices all around, as if those who sought to take advantage of others' peril to feast on them. At this point, we could only be extremely careful and urge our horses upwards. By the time we reached the flat ground at the summit, both men and horses were drenched in sweat. At 10:30 AM, we crossed the Jiezhi River and arrived at Jiezhi River Town. There were only a few residents in the town, and it was very desolate. The river was narrow and swift. I and Mr. Ou threw large stones into the middle of the stream to create stepping stones for those who followed, so that they would not have to wade barefoot. Half an hour later, the entire group gradually arrived. Everyone ate cold, filling-less steamed buns beside the stone table to appease their hunger, which was quite a unique experience.

At 12:30 PM, we whipped our horses again and set off. On the way, we talked about Liu Zhengheng, the magistrate of Luochuan County, who had graduated from Peking University, possessed considerable talent, and whose ambition extended beyond the county. An hour later, we thought that it was only 45 li from Jiezhi River to Fu County. Considering the time, we expected to arrive in Fu County for rest around 3:30 PM. Unexpectedly, after one mountain was crossed, another appeared. Climbing mountains and crossing ridges was no less difficult than the "Nose of Yama." Soon, we were traveling along a small path on the side of the mountain, with loose, scattered stones that made it easy for the horses to stumble. Looking down, there were jagged rocks and precipitous cliffs. The murmuring sound of the Luo River seemed to warn the travelers to proceed with caution. Around 4:30 PM, we finally arrived in Fu County, where Magistrate Jia Keqin and others were waiting by the Luo River to greet us. After we reached the other shore, we entered the city to rest. Mr. Jia and others went to the main road to welcome the members of the group who were riding in litters. Because the journey was arduous, they arrived in a continuous stream until dusk. That evening, everyone felt extremely exhausted, having traveled at least a hundred li or more. Six or seven out of ten went to bed and snored after dinner, unlike their previous energetic selves.

Although Fu County has mineral resources, most of them are undeveloped. In the short and hurried time available, it was difficult to search for and investigate materials. Therefore, we decided to leave Fu County for Ganquan the next morning (the 26th). We heard that the road was very flat, unlike the soul-stirring journey in Luochuan and Fu County.

Never Knowing the Taste of Fish in Their Lives

On the evening of the 25th, Magistrate Jia told me that there were no fish in Fu County, and the residents hardly knew the taste of fish in their lives. Even in places that were farther away, where a small amount of fish was obtained, the length was no more than two or three inches. The residents were even less familiar with how to cook and eat fish. Therefore, the taste was not very palatable, and the fish bones often pierced the throats of the people of Fu. Some people of Fu were even afraid of eating fish. Other situations are as follows: (A) Mineral Products (1) There are two coal mines: one is in Niuwu Town, forty li east of the city, with the best terrain. The coal is mostly lumpy, hard, and black, covering an area of about ten li, with reserves of about thirty trillion tons. The mine was once mined, producing more than five hundred tons per year. After the ninth year of the Republic of China, it was stopped due to local disturbances. The second is in Zhang Village, sixty li west of the city, and Liushi'an, seventy li west of the city, each covering an area of about twenty square li. Mining was stopped because the villagers were misled by feng shui beliefs. (2) Tongchuan Mine, twelve li north of the city, is located in Taihe Mountain. Because it has not yet been mined, the details are unknown. (3) The silver mine is located in Shichangzi, two hundred li northwest of the county. It is said that the composition is extremely good, with about seventy jin of silver in every hundred jin of ore. In the past, people from Sichuan went there to mine, but failed due to lack of scientific methods. (4) The iron mine is located in Jiangjiachuan Town, Xichuan, sixty li north of the county. The area also produces coal.

(B) Agricultural Products: The county has a total of 347,811 mu of land, of which 2,000 mu are planted with barley, with a total harvest of eighty shi; 5,000 mu with wheat, yielding four hundred shi; 2,000 mu with beans, yielding sixty shi; and millet, 5

Page 14

thousands [misprinted number, probably meant to be fifty-seven thousand] , yielding 2,850 shi. Millet, 58,000 mu, yielding two 900 shi [inconsistent number, likely misprint. 2900 is likely]. Yellow beans, 3,000 mu, yielding one hundred and twenty shi; corn, 16,000 mu, yielding eight hundred shi; wheat, 7,000 mu, yielding two hundred and eighty shi; sorghum, 124,000 mu, yielding 3,820 shi. This is the general overview of the county's agricultural products. This year's land tax is estimated to be about 16,000 to 17,000 yuan. The people's livelihood is declining, especially among farmers. Many have abandoned their farmland and fled elsewhere.

(C) Others: The total population of the county is about 30,000, with about four hundred more men than women. Most of the residents from other provinces are from Sichuan and Shandong. Religions include Catholicism and Protestantism. There is a carpet weaving factory in the city, producing high-quality and inexpensive products. There are also many furs, such as sheep, fox, leopard, and wolf. Other situations are mostly the same as in nearby counties. There is a senior primary school in the city with about seventy or eighty students, a junior primary school for girls with about thirty students, and a junior primary school (for boys) with about one hundred and twenty students. In addition, there are sixteen other junior primary schools, located in various townships and towns. The annual education budget is about six to seven thousand yuan. Teachers' salaries are about ten to fifteen yuan per month. Tuition is free, but a sports fee and miscellaneous fee of fifty cents each are required per semester.

The Luo River flows down from Ganquan County, passing around the east gate of the city to the south. When the water is high, it floods without limit, encroaching on farmland and affecting agricultural production. When the water is shallow, the riverbed dries up, which is insufficient for agricultural irrigation. Therefore, the Luo River in Shaanxi has a hundred harms and not a single benefit, which is worse than the Yellow River. On the eleventh of this month, the Luo River suddenly rose, with a water depth of more than thirty feet, threatening to flood Fu County. The residents were extremely frightened. Fortunately, it receded after half a day, otherwise, the damage would have been unimaginable.

When we were walking in the mountains, coal blocks were readily available. Heaven has given us such rich resources, but the transportation is as difficult as the Shu Road, resulting in goods being abandoned on the ground without anyone caring. Even if people with ambition raise funds to excavate, the transportation costs are very high. For example, the price of coal in Xi'an sometimes reaches fifty or sixty yuan per ton, which is almost twice as high as in Shanghai. Once there is competition, there is absolutely no value in winning. In short, if Shaanxi and other parts of China remain so difficult to cross, with no improvement in transportation, then even if there is gold everywhere, it is no different from dirt. Everyone who has set foot in Shaanxi and witnessed the environment here has the same feeling. I hope the government will pay attention to it. (Sent from Fu County on the morning of August 26th)

Several Wolves Ran Out

On the 26th, because Jia, the Magistrate of Fu County, insisted on keeping a photograph as a souvenir, we departed one hour later than usual. After the whole group crossed the Luo River, we walked along the lower slopes of the mountain for about four or five li before getting on our litters or other mounts. Looking at the time, it was already past eight o'clock. The road was indeed very flat that day. Wildflowers bloomed on both sides, and the flowering buckwheat in the fields was in full bloom, stretching endlessly like a light red carpet covering a green field, which was exceptionally beautiful. The mountains were green, and the flowers were lovely. There was no azure water or green waves to embellish the scenery, but there was nothing else lacking.

This was the first time since we set off from Xi'an that the sky was clear all day. Around one o'clock in the afternoon, the entire group arrived at Daozuobao after traveling fifty li. The rain was as fine as silk, and the temperature dropped significantly. In the litters, the cold wind blew on our faces. We realized that the grass in Guanzhong was not yet lush, but the weather already had the feeling of a cool autumn in September. Long-distance travelers with only a few layers of thin clothing knew that it would not be enough to keep them warm, and they gradually added cotton clothes along the way.

After setting off from Daozuobao, the flat ground and mountain slopes alternated. There was only one place on the mountain slope where the road was only a foot wide, and it was quite dangerous overlooking the ground below. Those sitting in litters mostly got out and walked to avoid accidents. Only Mr. Hu Juewen was soundly sleeping and did not jump down. I was also exhausted from traveling long distances during the day, desperately rushing to get to our next location, exchanging opinions with local people in the evening, and investigating the general situation of the newly arrived places. I would then work at my desk by candlelight or kerosene lamp until two or three in the morning before going to bed. I slept late and woke up early, and my spirits were extremely low. So I stayed curled up in my litter, letting nature take its course. Fortunately, everything went smoothly and we did not suffer any hardship. Along the way, we saw exposed coal seams on the mountainsides everywhere. Unfortunately, the coal seams were very thin, only one or two inches thick. Whether it was worth mining was also a question.

At 5:30 PM, we could see the city walls of Ganquan County in the distance. The county magistrate and others were already waiting outside the city to welcome us. Group leader Mr. Hu and others got out of their litters again, exchanged greetings with the welcomers, and expressed their gratitude. Then, we walked into Ganquan City. It was then that we realized that those who had slandered us before were inaccurate. Mr. Wei said to me with a smile, "Didn't you hear Director Zhao Shouyu's words in Xi'an? When the county magistrate was sitting in court on the city wall, he accidentally slapped the gavel, and several wolves ran out." Isn't that a description of Ganquan's desolation and lack of human presence? What is it like now? At the same time, when we were in Fu County, whenever we asked about the situation in Ganquan, they would shake their heads and say, "Not prosperous, not prosperous." So it is enough to prove that what we hear is not as accurate as what we see with our own eyes. That day happened to be a market day (the 5th, 15th, and 25th days of each lunar month are the days when goods from all directions gather in the market streets for trade). The roads were crowded and bustling, quite lively. Inferior goods were not yet extinct. Lion Brand toothpaste and Jintan with the logo of a mustached enemy were seen everywhere. However, there were no major economic figures. People in the county should also pay attention to this before our Northeast has been recovered.

The spring water in Ganquan County was very famous. It is said that the Empress Dowager Cixi of the Qing Dynasty used to get her drinking water from here, hence its fame. However, according to local people, the spring has now dried up. Others say that it is still a few miles outside the city, but the speakers could not describe it in detail, so there was no way to investigate. The water in Ganquan now is extremely turbid, far from its name.

There is Oil Underground

The biggest reason why the water in Ganquan is not very clean is that there are huge amounts of oil underground. Now, the people of Ganquan not only say that the Luo River contains alkali and cannot be used as good drinking water, but also that the well water has a layer of oil floating on the surface in normal cases, and in severe cases, it has a foul odor that is extremely unpleasant and absolutely cannot be used for making tea or cooking rice. According to County Magistrate Liu, the water near Ganquan is almost all like this, especially in the south, which proves that there is oil underground. In addition to oil, minerals such as coal and iron are also very famous. The iron mine is located in the Shigou area of Fucun Town, sixty li west of the county, and the quality is very good. In the first year of the Republic of China, local residents raised funds to mine it using indigenous methods, but the project was stopped due to insufficient funds and the impact of transportation barriers. The coal mine is located in Podi Village, fifteen li south of the county, and Yaodianzigou, eight li inside the city. The quality is not bad. After the Tongzhi Rebellion, it was suspended once. When it was reopened, it was affected by earthquakes and floods and could not continue. It has now become an abandoned mine. In addition to ordinary agricultural products, it produces medicinal materials such as licorice and Ruixian red, the amount of which is quite large, but there are no statistics available.

The county seat is located at the foot of a mountain, forming a triangle with a circumference of more than six li. The total area of the county is said to be 13,000 square li, with a population of more than 20,000. The annual revenue from land tax is about 2,000 yuan. There are more than one hundred households in the city, with about five or six hundred people. In terms of education, there are two senior primary schools, two junior primary schools for girls, and eighteen junior primary schools for boys, with a total of about five or six hundred students. The annual education expenditure is about five thousand yuan, all of which comes from local public funds. Teachers' salaries are only fifty yuan per year in junior primary schools and about one hundred and fifty yuan per year in senior primary schools. The curriculum is based on the temporary standards issued by the Ministry of Education. The senior primary schools do not have English classes.

At this point in the investigation, we should make a few points clear to the readers: In terms of prices, local merchants are mostly unwilling to tell the real numbers. Often, multiple inquiries are made for one type of price, and it is obtained after comparison, which cannot be considered completely accurate. This is one point. Our country lacks statistics, especially in the interior. The population area and mineral or other figures in one place are often different. The results of the investigation can only be considered a general situation and cannot be considered absolutely error-free. This is the second point. This investigation lasted only thirty days, covering a total of eighteen places. Almost two-thirds of the time was spent on the road. It was hurried and seemed like a fleeting glance. For a detailed investigation, even exploring one place would not be enough in months. Although we still need to perform chemical tests on the mineral samples we brought back after returning to Xi'an and other places, the time is still too short. This is the third point. That night, some members of the group were still plagued by fleas and could not sleep. The next morning (the 27th), we decided to depart for Fushi (the old Yan'an Prefecture), where we plan to stay for one or two days to explore the mining areas and wait for Mr. Huang Boda's arrival. Mr. Huang went alone to Yijun to investigate the mining areas in Yishicun and other places, but he has not caught up yet, and there is no way to transmit news. We are quite concerned. (Sent from Ganquan on the morning of August 27th)

Uncle Kou Fell 84

Mountain rain is coming, clothes and shoes are soaked. This was our situation when we left Ganquan at 7:30 AM on the 27th for Fushi. When each of us traveled west from our hometown, we all thought that there was little rain in this area, and Shaanxi was known for its drought, so there was no possibility of heavy rain. Therefore, very few people brought raincoats or umbrellas. When the rain came heavily, we felt that it was inappropriate to immediately enter the litters to avoid the rain while the welcomers were still standing by the roadside. Therefore, we had to brave the rain and walk slowly. After the welcomers dispersed, we each set off, and we had already suffered enough from the rain. We passed Laoshan at 10:30 AM, and the rain became heavier at 11:00 AM. The road was muddy and slippery, and the armed comrades and porters struggled greatly. We reached Jiuyan Mountain at 11:30 AM, and everyone dismounted to rest. We took the opportunity to eat tea and snacks to appease our hunger. At 12:00 PM, the whole group continued to move forward, but the rain still did not stop. Such persistent rain is rare in the north.

There were many interesting things that day. Before the entire group reached Laoshan, a man holding a rifle and wearing blue clothes suddenly emerged from the forest by the roadside. The sentry suspected that bandits had arrived and fired a shot. The man with the gun was startled, quickly put down his gun, and stated that he was a member of the security regiment. The soldiers hated that he should not have done so, and disarmed him. This is one thing. Mr. Xu Nairen of Central University is cautious in everything. Seeing people eating watermelon, Mr. Xu was worried that it was related to tiger plague, so he would say to the eater, "Be careful, be careful." Seeing swarms of flies about to fly, he would wave his hand and say, "Be careful, be careful." And he was very "careful" of all the members. So everyone called him "Uncle Hsu," Xu Yeshu. When we were about to arrive at Fushi at 5:00 PM that afternoon, the rope of the litter that Uncle Kou was riding in suddenly broke. Uncle Kou unexpectedly took a fall from the litter. After resting, Uncle Kou recalled the past and frowned and said, "Dangerous, dangerous." Seeing Uncle Kou's rather comical posture, everyone couldn't help but laugh. This is another thing.

At 5:30 PM, we could see the pagoda of Fushi in the litters. After a while, County Magistrate Shi and Public Security Bureau Chief Li came riding to greet us. Fushi is the former Yan'an Prefecture. Its scale is quite large, and its commerce is more prosperous than in the previous counties. When we entered the city, we were too tired from the journey, and the whole group would be working in Fushi for two days, so there was plenty of time. Therefore, we did not immediately start investigating.

Hunan Province Stores and Melts Inferior Copper Coins 85

Relieving Market Prices

To Maintain the Livelihood of the Common People

Changsha Dispatch: The Hunan Mint produces a large number of copper coins every year. However, due to the poor quality, the market price has gradually declined. In the recent year or so, one silver dollar can be exchanged for more than 6,800 copper coins. The downward trend is alarming. Provincial Chairman He Jian believes that if a way is not found to save these inferior copper coins, the future price will be unimaginable, and the livelihood of the common people will be even more affected. Therefore, he specifically proposed a discussion on relief methods at the Provincial Government Council, which was handed over to the Finance Committee to formulate a plan. The main idea is for the Provincial Bank to raise cash, buy up the copper coins for storage, and restrict the exchange coupons in the market to facilitate the circulation of copper coins. Since its implementation, it has achieved some success, and the market price of copper coins has gradually improved. However, although the market price of copper coins has slightly recovered, the cash spent by the Provincial Bank to buy the copper coins cannot recover its cost. If the purchased copper coins are re-used, the harm will still be the same. The only way to save them is to first melt the inferior copper coins into copper plates, and then use electroplating to plate them with pure copper. It is estimated that 300,000 strings of copper coins, totaling 300,000 pounds of copper, will only produce 90% of the original amount, leaving 270,000 pounds, totaling 1,025 shi. At a price of 37 yuan per shi, it can be sold for 74,925 yuan. The machinery, remaining materials, and by-products such as copper sulfate can still be sold to offset some of the expenses. After deducting the purchase price of the copper coins (50,000 yuan) and the equipment expenses and interest, a net profit of more than 9,500 yuan can be obtained. This method not only benefits the Provincial Bank with increased income, but also has the prospect of raising the market price of copper coins. The Provincial Government has now ordered active implementation, hoping to achieve the actual effect of relief in the shortest time. (September 8th)

Local Communications

Songjiang 86

Discussion on Raising Funds for a Shelter for Vagrants: This county does not yet have a shelter for vagrants, leading to ruffians and vagrants having no place to be accommodated, which poses a concern for public safety. Previously, various organizations advocated for the early establishment of a shelter for vagrants and the organization of a preparatory committee. Director Li Xian was elected as the chairman to expedite preparations. In addition to the funds already raised for the establishment of the shelter, there is still no foundation for the source of recurring expenses. After several meetings, it was decided to raise donations based on the following principles: (1) Shop donations, reformed from the elimination of donations to beggar gang leaders, collecting approximately 300 yuan per month; (2) Monthly donations from charitable organizations and wealthy households, collecting approximately 200 yuan per month; (3) Temporary special donations, from households with weddings, funerals, or celebrations, reformed from the cancellation of beggar gang leaders stationed at gates, and freeloaders soliciting fees. Weddings and celebrations will contribute two yuan, and funerals will contribute one yuan, with each section of the local township police responsible for reporting. This is estimated to collect approximately 100 yuan per month. Hereafter, beggar gang names are not allowed, and the suppression of the unemployed vagrants and beggars will be strict, with accommodation and vocational training provided. It is tentatively planned to accommodate 100 vagrants. Once the funding is more ample, the quota will be increased. The shelter's estimated monthly expenditure is a minimum of 600 yuan. The Public Security Bureau, district offices, and county chamber of commerce have jointly drafted detailed rules for raising funds and replied to the preparatory committee for implementation.

Recent News from the Red Cross Branch: Zhou Xuewen, from the Songjiang branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society, has achieved remarkable results since running the epidemic hospital stationed in Songjiang. Furthermore, Dr. Wang Peiyuan, the president of the society, has provided careful guidance on medical affairs, greatly benefiting the people of Songjiang. Dr. Ke Deqiong, the medical director of the society, has been dedicated to diagnosis and treatment day and night. Since the opening of the clinic on July 16, countless people have been saved. In addition to the subsidies from the society, there are also enthusiastic officials and gentry who voluntarily donate generously. Currently, County Magistrate Shen of Songjiang has donated 50 yuan, and Mrs. Zheng Bocang, the mother of Songjiang gentleman Zheng Bocang, has donated 100 yuan in the hope of a speedy recovery from illness. These donations have been forwarded to the society by Director Zhou. It is also heard that the hospital has decided at its fifth regular meeting to purchase land and build its own hospital buildings. Plans are now being drawn up, and preparations are actively underway.

Jiading 88

Theft of Guns and Ammunition from the Defense Corps: On the sixth night, around 11 PM, at the home of Shen Fuquan, a member of the second district, fourth jia defense corps in Xiyangjiacun, Nanxiang, suddenly five or six bandits, claiming to be communists, forced Shen to hand over firearms. Two rifles, over a hundred bullets, three yuan and eight jiao in silver, and a gold earring were stolen. Neighbors heard the commotion and shouted for help, causing the thieves to flee in panic. Nearby corps members gathered upon hearing the cries, surrounded and searched the area, but were unable to find them.

When they reached Bazhiqiao, the Public Security Bureau police officers and police team withdrew on their own accord. As a result, the families of Jin Desheng and Jin Wenhao in the forty-second tu of Rui were robbed of jewelry and silver totaling over four hundred yuan. Wuxi 89

Robbery on a Small Steamer Injures Passenger: The boats traveling between this county and Zhou Tieqiao, which is under the jurisdiction of Yixing County, departed from Yixing towards Wuxi yesterday morning around 3 AM as usual. Not long after setting off, four individuals resembling workers on the shore shouted to board the boat. The boat did not think much of it and allowed them to disembark after docking. The boat continued to sail. Unexpectedly, when the boat reached Songmaoqiao near Zhangshe, the four suddenly pretended to fight. Chen Genfu, the boat crew member, was about to go down to the cabin to investigate when he suddenly heard a loud bang. A bullet pierced the boat's plank. The crew and passengers, seeing this, knew they were being robbed and allowed the bandits to search and loot. More than ten passengers were spared nothing. In total, goods and cash worth approximately over two hundred yuan were robbed. After the bandits had finished looting, they fired another shot, hitting Chen Genfu, the boat crew member, in the left leg. Afterwards, the injured man was carried to Tongren Hospital for treatment. A loss report was filed with the county to request an investigation.

Abolition of the Salt Field Public Office: Feng Ruliang, the manager of the Liangzhe Inspection Branch, took over the anti-smuggling affairs of the entire Zhejiang last spring, renamed it the Tax Police, eliminated the weak and retained the strong, and saved a significant amount of funds. Letter

Letter from Wang Decheng and Guo Guangchang 98

Having just read a piece of Suzhou news under the headline "Investigation of the Case of Dereliction of Duty by a Judge in Wujin County" in the local news column of your newspaper on September 8, page 3, the content is completely inconsistent with the facts. Wei Yongquan is a clerk of this court. He has neither filed a complaint with the Ministry of Justice, nor has the Ministry of Justice dismissed us and handed us over to the Wu County District Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation. Although we did go to Suzhou on the sixth of this month to respond to the interrogation of the Wu District Court Prosecutor, it was because the former President of this Court, Lei Renlong, was accused of dereliction of duty, etc., to the Ministry of Justice, and we were summoned to testify in court. Our attendance in Suzhou was purely in the capacity of witnesses and had nothing to do with the case. The report in your newspaper is based on hearsay and is untrue. We hereby urgently request a correction to avoid confusion. With regards, Sincerely, Wang Decheng, Judge, and Guo Guangchang, Clerk, Wujin County Court, September 8.

Jiangsu Education Department Raises Middle School Standards (Continued) 102

Regarding education: (1) Teachers: 1. Teachers should follow the curriculum standards set by the Ministry of Education to develop teaching plans for the courses they teach, aiming to meet the minimum requirements for graduation. 2. Teachers should make full preparations before class and handle the course carefully and dynamically after class. 3. Teachers should provide students with sufficient practice and review for the courses they teach during class. They should be responsible for guiding students in self-study after class. 4. Teachers should follow the planned teaching order and proceed practically without wasting time. 5. Teachers should fully use teaching aids such as physical objects, instruments, specimens, and charts. 6. Teachers should guide students to make full use of reference materials. 7. Teachers should closely examine students' daily performance and find ways to promote their progress at any time. 8. Teachers should guide students in extracurricular and vacation assignments and various beneficial physical and mental activities. 9. Teachers should provide students with guidance on career choices or further education. (2) Students: 1. Students should make full use of self-study time for pre-class preparation and post-class review. 2. Students should submit practice papers on time. 3. Students should make full use of reference books and newspapers. 4. Students should organize extracurricular reading clubs and academic research clubs under the guidance of teachers. 5. Students should use vacations to carry out supplementary studies, investigations, data collection, and research activities. 6. Students should submit reading notes and research reports to the respective teachers for evaluation and publication. 7. Students should select teachers to guide them and pay attention to preparing for career choices or further education. Third, regarding the curriculum: (1) Language: 1. High school and junior high school should each have a three-year specific plan for selecting teaching materials. This plan should not change with teachers. 2. Each semester, about 30 model essays should be selected for teaching. In addition to in-depth study of the content, key sentences must be extracted. 3. Within three years of high school, 10 books should be designated for close reading. Within three years of junior high school, 6 books should be designated for close reading. Each semester, several books should be assigned for extracurricular reading and term-end skimming, the selection standards of which are determined by each school according to the curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education. 4. Students should submit reading notes for each two weeks, which are evaluated and returned by the teachers. 5. Regular tests on selected texts, close reading, and skimming, and occasional competitions such as essay writing, essay collection, and speech. 6. Junior high school students write an essay once a week, and high school students write an essay once every two weeks. Junior high school students submit papers in class, and high school students submit papers in class every other time, all of which are set by the teacher. (2) Mathematics: 1. Cultivate students' abilities and habits such as rigorous thinking, neat calculations, and precise drawings. 2. Teachers must ensure that students practice the basic methods of mathematics proficiently. 3. For homework after class in high school and junior high school, problems should be assigned with a deadline for submission, reviewed, and strictly corrected. 4. Hold oral exams and short-time temporary tests every week in junior high school and focus on blackboard exercises. 5. Guide students to refer to books and newspapers, and review notes from time to time to give usual scores. 6. Organize extracurricular research groups to arouse interest in learning mathematics. (3) English: 1. Students in the first and second grades of junior high school should practice making sentences every week. 2. Students in all grades of junior high school and high school should write an essay once every two weeks. 3. Encourage students to use English conversation in high school English classes and teach directly in English as much as possible. 4. Students should review the vocabulary in the textbook by themselves with the dictionary. 5. Practice the text, often using methods such as dictation, writing, memorizing, analyzing long sentences, explaining grammar, and applying new words to form sentences. 6. Grammar should be taught separately in high school. 7. High school students should be assigned extracurricular reading materials. 8. Organize English conversation, reading newspapers, and other activities. 9. Often hold oral short-time tests and occasionally competitions such as essay writing, essay collection, and speech. (4) Social Sciences: 1. Compile and select appropriate textbooks for each subject and supplement teaching materials. 2. Encourage students to carry out the following extracurricular activities: A. Making charts; B. Making research topics; C. Making investigation, visit, statistical, and comparative reports; D. Researching current affairs and social issues or setting limits for presentation on current affairs topics; E. Discussion meeting. 3. Grade student notes and homework reports. 4. Often hold short-time tests. 5. Special history and geography classrooms must pay attention to arousing youth's national self-confidence. (5) Natural Science: 1. Sufficiently utilize physical objects, instruments, specimens, charts, etc. during class so that students can observe directly. 2. Students must have a suitable place and sufficient equipment for self-experiments. Before and during biological, physical, and chemical experiments, teachers must use scientific methods to provide sufficient hints and detailed guidance to arouse their interest in automatic observation and research. 4. After the experiment, students must use a faithful attitude, apply learning to cautiously study and make detailed reports. 5. Each subject's teaching must, within the possible scope, use the method of first experimenting and then lecturing to allow students to practice using induction. 6. Focus on the science applied in production and national defense. 7. After each unit is taught, students must be given a large number of thought-provoking calculation and Q&A questions for practice. 8. Fully encourage extracurricular work such as collecting, manufacturing, traveling, visiting, competitions, exhibitions, making charts, research reports, organizing research societies, etc. 9. Often hold oral tests and unscheduled tests. 10. Grade student notebooks, draft exercise books, and evaluate experiment reports on schedule. (End)
