National Chinan University to Begin Classes Tomorrow 104

The Zhenru Campus Has Been Renovated and Looks Brand New

丨President Zheng Exerts His Utmost Efforts in Reconstruction

After the outbreak of the Shanghai War, National Chinan University established schools in Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Suzhou to prevent the interruption of overseas Chinese education. The results achieved were remarkable. Subsequently, after the ceasefire agreement was established, President Zheng devoted all his efforts to the reconstruction movement. The school buildings and teaching equipment in Zhenru that had been bombed and damaged by the Japanese army were repaired, restored, and purchased one by one, resulting in a completely new and impressive appearance. The cost was worth tens of thousands of dollars. To save expenses and for convenience, President Zheng specially purchased a diesel engine with more than forty horsepower as a generator. All the school's electric lights and running water are self-supplied, no longer relying on the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company. At the same time, to expand the business and develop culture, the university also established its own printing press, purchasing printing machines and lead type. All the school's published books, magazines, lecture notes, and all documents can be printed in-house. The school suffered significant losses during the war, but was able to restore its original state in the shortest possible time, and from there, to further expand and develop. The scale is grand and the equipment is complete, which is truly rare. This is the result of President Zheng's painstaking management over the past few months. The school buildings have long been renovated and classes began on September 1st. The office on Hardoon Road in Shanghai was moved back before September 1st. The departments of major and secondary schools in Guangdong Province and the secondary school department in Suzhou are also continuing to move back. Secretary-General Yang Yufen, Dean of the College of Liberal Arts Chen Zhongfan, Dean of the College of Commerce Ye Yuan, Dean of the College of Science Yu Jitai, and Director of the Secondary School Department Kuang Songling, have been supervising the faculty and staff to devote themselves to the progress of school affairs and teaching affairs, which is very orderly. All new and old students paid fees, registered, and selected courses on schedule, and the opening ceremony is scheduled for 7:00 a.m. on September 12th, with formal classes beginning that day. In order to adapt to the needs of the post-war environment and improve efficiency, the courses offered by the school are all important, with very little duplication. Freshmen in the university department do not distinguish between colleges, and sophomores do not distinguish between departments, but specialize in common required basic courses. Only after the third year will they conduct specialized research to explore advanced knowledge. The secondary school department temporarily has two departments: normal and vocational, and will no longer set up a business department separately, but will open business courses. After all teachers and students of the school moved back to the original Zhenru campus, their spirits were exceptionally happy. Everyone is focusing on school affairs, teaching affairs, and academic work, which is truly a very good phenomenon.

Zhengfeng College of Liberal Arts Plans After Establishment 105

Adding Departments of Political Economy and Art

Since its establishment this year, Zhengfeng College of Liberal Arts on Jiaozhou Road in this city, under the leadership of its President, the literary figure Mr. Wang Xishen, in order to live up to the Ministry of Education's promotion of education and to comfort the students' enthusiasm for learning, has engaged in expansion, adding departments of political economy and art. Mr. Zhu Xiangwan, a master of Chinese studies, has been hired as the director of the Department of Literature, lawyer Chen Tingrui as the director of the Department of Political Economy, and former Central University professor Wu Gaiting as the director of the Department of Art. In addition, former Jiangsu Education Director Jiang Zhuzhuang, former Civil Affairs Director Hu Pu'an, Guanghua University professor Qian Jibo, history expert Lü Simian, traditional Chinese painter Huang Zihong, and former Central University traditional Chinese painting director Lü Fengzi have been hired to take charge of various subjects. Other professors are also among the best of their time. Therefore, the number of applicants has been very enthusiastic, and the freshman class of the Department of Literature has already exceeded the original quota. It is also heard that Mr. Wu Gaiting, the director of the Department of Art, mainly focuses on the study of traditional Chinese painting and sculpture, with the study of Western painting as preparation for the improvement of traditional Chinese painting. However, in view of the fact that most art schools in Shanghai tend to emphasize ideals and neglect application, and students feel the pain of having no way out after graduation, it is planned to focus on crafts and educational ability, with the aim of creating practical talents to meet the needs of the current society, and it is planned to officially name it the Department of Art Education, which is truly good news for the art world in our country.

Teachers and Staff of the Women's Department of East China Middle School 106

A Banquet in Honor of Zhou Feicheng and Chen Bai

Since its establishment, the Women's Department of East China Middle School on Baylor Road has achieved remarkable results. The teachers hired are all famous figures of their time. Recently, two teachers from the school, Mr. Zhou Feicheng and Mr. Chen Bai, were appointed as chiefs of the Second and Fourth Sections of the Municipal Education Bureau. All colleagues in the school were delighted and specially held a banquet at the Atlantic Restaurant last night to congratulate them. In addition to the two section chiefs Zhou and Chen, more than 20 people attended the banquet, including the principal of the school, Ma Jiazhen, and teachers and staff. During the banquet, the development plan of the school was discussed in detail. As for the registration procedures, they will be completed soon.

Establishment of the Yefeng Painting Society 107

The Yefeng Painting Society in the Park District of Jiangwan Road is organized by a group of young people engaged in art, who feel the decline of art in recent times and the high cost of school life. Its purpose is to study correct techniques and theories, to find ways for art lovers who have dropped out of school to continue their studies, and to provide correct guidance for people who want to learn to draw. It is divided into Western painting group, woodcut group, sculpture group, pattern group, and cartoon group. The guidance is effective, and the aim is to gain a correct understanding in the shortest possible time. It is currently widely seeking like-minded people.

Lawn Tennis Senior Singles Qiu, Lin, Zheng, De Enter Semi-Finals 109

Qiu Feihai Zheng Zhaojia De Foe

All Won the Right to the Semi-Finals Yesterday

丨Qiu Feihai Meets Lin Baohua in the Semi-Finals丨

The senior singles competition of the Lawn Tennis Club was completed yesterday. Qiu Feihai, De Foe, Zheng Zhaojia, and Lin Baohua won the right to the semi-finals. In the semi-finals, Qiu will meet Lin, and Zheng will meet De Foe. Yesterday, the two groups of Qiu Feihai vs. Jiang Daozhang and De Foe vs. Kanafanluo were held at the French Chamber of Commerce, and Zheng Zhaojia vs. Yu Tianguang was held at the China Tennis Court.

Qiu Feihai Wins Against Jiang Daozhang

丨6-1, 6-1, 6-1丨

Qiu and Jiang started fighting at 2:45 PM. Because the situation of victory or defeat was very different, the shots were extremely casual. In the three sets, only two or three games had several spectacular shots. Both of them were flat-hitting on the baseline. It was also rare for Qiu to have deep and corner shots. In the first set, Jiang won one game by returning Qiu's powerful shot in the fifth game. In the second set, Jiang won one game in the third game, and in the third set, he won one game in the second game.

De Foe Wins Against Kanafanluo

丨6-2, 6-1, 4-6, 6-4丨

De and Ka then took the stage. De Foe still used a big-knife-axe-like attack of one shot and one kill. The first two sets were like breaking bamboo. By the third set, the clever Kanafanluo seemed to have seen through De's weakness and attacked De's backhand continuously, attacking the same side from near and far, left and right, and blocking and killing on the net. De Foe was exhausted from running around, and his strength gradually weakened. Although De Foe took the lead with a score of 4-3, he was still taken back by Ka for three consecutive games, winning a set. In the fourth set, Ka once took the lead with a score of 2-1. After that, the score was tied at 3-3 and 4-4. In the ninth game, Ka took the lead with a score of 3-1, and there was a great chance of winning this set again, but he was eventually reversed by De and won the whole game. De's victory took a lot of effort, and the number of self-inflicted balls was high. The backhand was not at all certain. Many shots aimed at the left and right sides went out of bounds, and he has regressed a lot compared to last year. Therefore, Zheng Zhaojia has a good chance of winning.

Zheng Zhaojia Wins Against Yu Tianguang

Zheng Zhaojia played against Yu Tianguang at the China Tennis Court yesterday. The two young players were formally playing each other for the first time yesterday. Yu was the champion of the open B group of the Shanghai Lawn Tennis Club in 1930, while Zheng was a well-known emerging athlete. This year's technology has made special progress. Under the battle, the levels were very different. Zheng's strength was hard and strong, while Yu's was relatively weak. Zheng's shots often made Yu unable to run, the situation was loose, and there was very little brilliance. Yu also had good performances when he went to the net to block shots. After Zheng won three games in the first set, Zheng served and won three consecutive points, but still failed. Yu served and won one game, and in the next game Zheng failed with a wild ball, making it 4-2. Zheng added two more games and won the first set with 6-2. After a short rest, they changed new balls to chase each other. The spirits of the two of them suddenly improved, and the competition felt more intense, and the situation became very tense. But soon Yu showed a weak state again. Yu won the third and sixth games, and Zheng won again with 6-2. Zheng then entered the semi-finals, and his opponent was the defending champion De Foe.

Chairman Lin Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 115

Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai Pay a Visit

Accompanied by Mayor Wu in the Afternoon to Visit Wang

Chairman of the National Government Lin Sen arrived in Shanghai on the Jianghua ship of the China Merchants Bureau from Xun at 10:00 AM yesterday. He disembarked at the Jinliyuan Wharf and went directly to his residence on Jin Shenfu Road to rest. At noon, Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai both visited him. In the afternoon, accompanied by Mayor Wu, he visited Wang. According to Chairman Lin, he came here for medical treatment. Wang Jingwei is always extremely responsible and will never be negative. He himself will return to Nanjing in about three or four days, etc. The details are recorded as follows:

Situation of Arrival The Jianghua ship docked at the Jinliyuan Wharf on the Bund at 10:00 AM yesterday. In advance, armed policemen from the Public Security Bureau and detectives from the French Concession were on guard around the area. Wen Hongen, Director of the Public Security Bureau, and Lu Ying, Captain of the Detective Team, etc., all personally came to direct the operation. The military band of the Public Security Bureau also played music at the wharf. Those who went to welcome him included Mayor Wu, and more than 20 of Lin's relatives, etc. After the Jianghua docked, Mayor Wu and others boarded the Jianghua and met Lin in the dining room. After a brief exchange of greetings, they disembarked. Lin and Mayor Wu returned to their residence by car. Not long after, Jiao Hongen, accompanied by Inspector General Gong Xikui, and Huang Jusu, etc., came to visit. They left soon after. At 11:40, Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai arrived and went inside to talk for an hour before leaving. Lin went out to visit Wang at 2:00 PM and returned to his residence in the evening.

Lin's Talk Lin was wearing a blue gown and black leather shoes yesterday. Although his temples were gray, his spirit was vigorous. Lin met with reporters from various newspapers in the dining room of the ship. The reporter (asked) Did Mr. Lin come to Shanghai to meet Mr. Wang to urge him to return to Nanjing? (Answer) I came to Shanghai to consult Dr. Lu Zhong'an of the Central Sanatorium because the ointment I took to Lushan last time was damp and unusable. I have also been suffering from asthma recently, so I came here for medical treatment. Mr. Wang is sick and I will visit him. There is no such thing as urging or comforting. I believe that after Mr. Wang's illness is cured, he will be able to return to Nanjing. (Asked) Zhang Hanqing does not leave North China and the military branch is still presided over by Zhang in reality after the change. It is rumored that Wang is negative, which seems to be the case. Is this true? (Answer) The North China Military Branch has been established and is temporarily responsible by Zhang. Wang's stay in Shanghai is entirely due to his illness. Mr. Wang has always been extremely responsible. The saying of negativity is not true. (Asked) When will Mr. Lin return to Nanjing? (Answer) I will stay in Shanghai for three or four days and then return to Nanjing.

Jiang and Cai Visit Lin Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai visited Lin at his residence at 11:40 yesterday and left at 12:35. When reporters asked Jiang and Cai about the results of their meeting with Lin, Jiang said, I have not met Chairman Lin for a long time, so I came to visit. I have not decided whether to return to Fujian on the 14th. I probably will not go to Hankou. I will take a boat back to Fujian as soon as there is one. Cai said that the visit to Lin was also a normal visit, because Lin is the Chairman of the National Government, and there were no other important matters. Probably the matter concerns military and political affairs, so it is inconvenient to publish.

Meeting Wang in the Afternoon Lin left his residence at 2:00 PM in the afternoon, and his whereabouts were quite secret. However, at 4:30 PM in the afternoon, Lin and Mayor Wu took four cars separately, passed through Qi Qi Road to Fenglin Bridge, turned west, and met Wang at Wang's secret residence. Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai were also not at the residence in the afternoon.

Japanese Plainclothes Police Activity in the French Concession 117

Recorded in Two Western Newspapers

A Chinese Person Arrested

The Greater Shanghai Evening Post said that the French Consulate is preparing a protest note to be sent to the Japanese Consulate, formally protesting the case of Japanese plainclothes police officers arresting Chinese people in the French Concession yesterday. The content of the case is that many Japanese police officers, traveling in a car, without first obtaining the permission of the French authorities, went to a restaurant opened by a Korean on Luban Road No. 13 to arrest people. When they arrived, the restaurant was closed. The Korean owner was out. The Japanese police arrested a Chinese person inside the restaurant. When an Annamite patrolman heard the news, he invited several French patrolmen to rush to the scene, but the Chinese person had already been taken away. Only three plainclothes Japanese police officers were detained and taken back to the police station. Later, the Japanese Consulate sent someone to come and take the three people away.

The Shanghai Times said that yesterday afternoon, an incident almost developed into a conflict between the patrolmen and the Japanese plainclothes police in the French Concession. The French consular authorities will protest to the Japanese side. The inside story and intention of this matter are not yet clear, but the methods used have greatly angered the French Concession officials. At about 2:00 PM yesterday, ten Japanese police officers, all in plain clothes, (according to the Continental News, the three people detained were wearing Chinese clothes), either in cars or other vehicles, met in front of a restaurant opened by a Korean on Luban Road No. 10. At that time, the restaurant was closed, and the owner was out, leaving only the hostess and a Chinese maid, and the maid's brother inside. The Japanese entered the room and asked the maid about the owner, but they could not find him, so they went upstairs together. At that time, a Chinese detective happened to pass by and saw the situation, so he quickly sounded the alarm, summoning many Annamite patrolmen. However, the Japanese had already kidnapped the maid's brother and drove away in a car. The Annamite patrolmen and others then detained three Japanese and took them back to the police station. Then, the Japanese Consulate sent someone to come and take them away. As for the Chinese person, he had not been released by the time this newspaper went to press. According to the French police station, the owner of the restaurant, a Korean, is a law-abiding citizen who has worked for the tram company for several years.

According to this newspaper's news, the incident happened the day before yesterday. When this newspaper received the news, it sent a reporter to the French police station to inquire, but because the chief patrol was not met, the details were not obtained, so it was inconvenient to publish. The reporter again inquired from all parties yesterday and learned that when the detectives searched No. 13 that day, a Chinese person was indeed arrested by the Japanese detectives, escorted into a car, and rushed away. However, everyone said that they did not know where he was being held. However, it was heard that the detained Chinese person, named Zhang Zhenxian, was from Hunan, and was a relative of the maid at No. 13. He was mistakenly detained because he went to visit.

The Ministry of Finance Held a Lottery Yesterday in Shanghai for the Redemption of Seven Types of Public Bonds 118

24 Treasury Bonds Will Be Paid Out Starting on the 20th

The Rest Will Be Paid Out Starting at the End of This Month

The Ministry of Finance held a lottery yesterday at the Bankers' Association on Hong Kong Road for the redemption of seven types of public bonds, from 2:00 PM to 3:10 PM. The public bonds included the seventh redemption of the Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bonds, the eleventh redemption of the Sixth Year of the Republic of China 6% Public Bonds, the eleventh redemption of the Fourteenth Year of the Republic of China Public Bonds, the tenth redemption of the National Government Ministry of Finance Rehabilitation Short-Term Public Bonds, the eighth redemption of the Seventeenth Year of the Republic of China Financial Short-Term Public Bonds, the ninth redemption of the Eighteenth Year of the Republic of China Disaster Relief Public Bonds, and the seventh redemption of the Nineteenth Year of the Republic of China Customs Duty Public Bonds. Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance, representing Chairman Zheng Lai, gave a report, and many concerned guests from all walks of life attended. The details are as follows:

Attendees: Chairman Song, representing Director Zheng Lai of the Ministry of Finance's Public Debt Department; Supervisors Yang Tizhi of the Auditing Department, Wang Songling of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Fan Ketang of the Foundation Committee, Wang Xinguan of the Bankers' Association, Fu Songnian of the Money Trade Association; Lottery Drawers Li Tisheng of the Central Bank, Zhu Qisong of the Bank of China, Wei Bo of the Bank of Communications; Administrators Huang Guoen, Dong Puming, He Xiaojuan, Liang Yaozong; Recorders Chen Shaochao, You Yiti, Ji Juncai; Document Clerks Huang Qizong, Xu Zumo, Huang Meizhao; Receptionists Zheng Yijian, Chen Jian; and approximately one hundred other concerned guests from various sectors.

Chairman's Report: At 2:00 PM, the lottery began. Chairman Zheng Lai first delivered a report, stating: "Today is the date for the lottery to redeem the Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bonds and seven other types of bonds. We are delighted that you have all come to observe. I will briefly report on the history of each type of bond to you all. (1) The Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bonds were issued in the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, with a total value of 2.4 million yuan. They have already been redeemed six times, and this is the seventh redemption, with one winning ticket to be drawn, worth 24,000 yuan. (2) The Sixth Year of the Republic of China 6% Public Bonds were issued with a total value of 45 million yuan. They have already been redeemed ten times, and this is the eleventh redemption, with one winning ticket to be drawn, worth 450,000 yuan. (3) The Fourteenth Year of the Republic of China Public Bonds were issued with a total value of 15 million yuan. They have already been redeemed ten times, and this is the eleventh redemption, with one winning ticket to be drawn, worth 150,000 yuan. (4) The National Government Ministry of Finance Rehabilitation Short-Term Public Bonds were issued in the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, with a total value of 40 million yuan. They have already been redeemed nine times, and this is the tenth redemption, with two winning tickets to be drawn, worth 800,000 yuan. (5) The Seventeenth Year of the Republic of China Financial Short-Term Public Bonds were issued with a total value of 30 million yuan. They have already been redeemed seven times, and this is the eighth redemption, with ten winning tickets to be drawn, worth 3 million yuan. (6) The Eighteenth Year of the Republic of China Disaster Relief Public Bonds were issued with a total value of 10 million yuan. They have already been redeemed eight times, and this is the ninth redemption, with one winning ticket to be drawn, worth 100,000 yuan. (7) The Nineteenth Year of the Republic of China Customs Duty Public Bonds were issued with a total value of 20 million yuan. They have already been redeemed six times, and this is the seventh redemption, with one winning ticket to be drawn, worth approximately 200,000 yuan. All of the winning bonds mentioned above, except for the Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bonds, which are scheduled to begin payment on September 20th, the remaining six types of bonds are scheduled to begin payment on September 30th. All principal amounts due for winning bonds, along with the accrued interest on each bond, will be paid by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in various locations. Please have the supervisors verify the winning tickets and the ticket stubs in order to proceed with the lottery."

Winning Numbers: After the Chairman finished his report, he immediately instructed the lottery drawers to proceed with the lottery. After drawing the winning tickets, the lottery drawers first presented the tickets to the Chairman for inspection, then handed them over to the supervisors for verification. Once verified, the winning numbers were displayed on a board, while the recorders registered the numbers. The supervisors also verified the winning ticket numbers and stamped the ticket stubs to certify their authenticity. The numbers, types, quantities, and amounts of the winning tickets will soon be published in the "Ministry of Finance Daily" and various newspapers in and outside of Beijing to inform the public. The winning numbers from yesterday are listed below: one ticket for Austrian Indemnity Public Bonds, number 13; one ticket for Sixth Year of the Republic 6% Public Bonds, number 19; one ticket for Fourteenth Year of the Republic Public Bonds, number 53; two tickets for Ministry of Finance Rehabilitation Public Bonds, numbers 07 and 33; ten tickets for Seventeenth Year Financial Short-Term Public Bonds, numbers 06, 19, 30, 40, 44, 60, 62, 76, 83, and 94; one ticket for Eighteenth Year Disaster Relief Public Bonds, number 55; one ticket for Nineteenth Year Customs Duty Public Bonds, number 53.

Okano Arrives in Shanghai: The Geneva International League of Nations Conference is about to convene. Lieutenant Commander Okano Toshikichi, a naval aide to the Japanese plenipotentiary to the League of Nations, has been stationed in China for a relatively long time, is familiar with the situation in China, and is fluent in Chinese. During the Liaoning Incident, he served as a military attache stationed in Shanghai and is the author of the book "Talks on China". This time, the Japanese Ministry of the Navy dispatched him as an aide to the League of Nations Conference, instructing him to come to Shanghai from Japan to gather materials on the Manchurian Incident and the situation of Chinese boycotts. Okano arrived in Shanghai yesterday aboard the Shanghai Maru. Japanese naval officials in Shanghai, such as Commander Sugita, Lieutenant Commander Okino, Captain Kitaoka, and Commander Yamaguchi, welcomed him at the Huishan Wharf. Upon landing, Okano went to the Atago warship to visit Commander Sakano and discuss the data on the Manchurian and Shanghai cases to be presented at the League of Nations Conference. According to Okano, he decided to travel to Europe via Siberia and is scheduled to leave Shanghai on the 13th of this month. He will also need to visit the puppet authorities in the Northeast to gather materials to take to Geneva.

Hirata Returns to Shanghai: Lieutenant Commander Hirata Masaharu, the Japanese naval attache stationed in Shanghai, also returned to Shanghai on the same ship as Okano yesterday. According to Hirata, speaking to Japanese reporters, Japan must do its utmost to protect the rights it has already acquired in various parts of China under the current situation. The entire nation is now united in recognizing that the government and the military have reached a consensus on taking decisive action regarding the phenomenon in the Yangtze River and Southeast regions that is detrimental to Japan. Only in this way can Japan survive.

Representative of the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese Army Zheng Guilin Arrives in Shanghai 120

Negotiating Assistance for a Large-Scale Offensive

Visited Feng Yuxiang in Tai'an

Zheng Guilin, commander of the 48th Route Army of the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army, dispatched Chief of Staff Wang Youmei and Chief Counselor Ma Jun as representatives to enter the pass and seek aid in the south due to a lack of troops, ammunition, and clothing. The representatives arrived in Shanghai by train yesterday morning. A reporter from the Datong News Agency interviewed them at the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association and inquired about the combat situation of Zheng's troops, their journey south, and their mission. The following is an account of their conversation. According to the representatives, Zheng's troops consist of 20,000 men with over 8,000 guns, stationed near a certain place. Two weeks ago, they attacked Huludao but withdrew due to insufficient ammunition. As the weather is getting colder and the soldiers are still wearing single-layer clothing, and ammunition is also lacking, they are unable to launch a large-scale offensive. In the future, when the sorghum is harvested and the green gauze tent is lost as cover, combat will inevitably be more difficult. Therefore, Commander Zheng sent them to enter the pass and seek aid in the south, hoping that all sectors would find ways to provide assistance. They stated that they departed from their station on the 27th of last month, went on foot to Beidaihe, took the Beining Railway into the pass, transferred to the Jinpu Railway south, and when passing through Tai'an on the 6th of this month, they got off the train and stayed for one night. The next morning, they went to the Puzhao Temple on Mount Tai to visit Mr. Feng Yuxiang and had lunch at Feng's place. However, Mr. Feng was suffering from a toothache and his right cheek was quite swollen, so when they described the situation outside the pass, Mr. Feng kept crying but did not speak. They went down the mountain at 3:00 PM and took a train to Nanjing, where they reported to the Military Affairs Commission, the Executive Yuan, and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and requested assistance, which was satisfactory. They then took a train from Nanjing last night and arrived in Shanghai this morning (i.e., yesterday). In the coming days, they plan to contact various sectors in Shanghai to seek assistance and hope that all sectors will provide effective assistance. It is learned that the Support Association has planned to submit a proposal to the Standing Council to discuss assistance measures.

Executive Committee of the Anti-Opium Society Resolves to Fight the Jiangsu Province Opium Monopoly 123

The China National Anti-Opium Society held its first executive committee meeting for the ninth year yesterday at 3:00 PM at the Hua'an Building on Jing'an Temple Road. All committee members except those not in Shanghai attended the meeting, including Wang Jingqi, Li Denghui, Shen Junru, Lin Kanghou, Yin Yongfu, Xu Jigong, Ding Shujing, Guo Bao-yi, Yan Yuheng (representing Li Fengchu), and Zhao Yi (representing Xu Jigong). Wang Jingqi was publicly elected as chairman and Dong Wenyuan as recorder. The meeting began with the usual formalities. First, Chairman Wang Jingqi delivered a speech, welcoming the new committee members. Then, Secretary-General Huang Jia-hui reported on the proceedings of the representative assembly and the society's work. The discussion items then commenced: (A) A request to the government for strict prohibition of opium. Resolved: To submit ten suggestions and request the government to implement them earnestly: (1) Permanently abolish the opium monopoly policy; (2) Opium prohibition should be based on the principle of complete eradication; (3) Allocate opium prohibition fines to be used for handling opium prohibition and anti-drug expenses; (4) The government's opium prohibition should cooperate with the people; (5) To strictly enforce opium prohibition, it is necessary to punish corrupt officials first; (6) Conduct an opium scourge investigation, with the people responsible; (7) Designate Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Henan, and Shandong provinces as model areas for opium prohibition; (8) Strictly manage narcotics; (9) Pay attention to the selection of personnel responsible for handling opium prohibition agencies; (10) Hire international experts and adopt good laws from various countries. (B) Protest against the Jiangsu opium monopoly. Resolved: The society will periodically initiate invitations to Jiangsu gentry to jointly devise countermeasures and pledge not to compromise until the goal of abolition is achieved. (C) Fundraising. Resolved: To organize an economic committee and invite enthusiastic anti-drug leaders from all sectors to serve as committee members and solicit funds in groups. All important cases resolved today have been entrusted to the secretariat for separate implementation as soon as possible to achieve rapid results. The meeting adjourned at about 5:00 PM.

Public Memorial Service Held at the People's Grand Auditorium

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends a Letter to the Telegraph Office Requesting Exemption from International Telegraph Fees 126

The Public Welfare Should be Considered

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the International Telegraph Office yesterday, requesting exemption from international telegraph fees to benefit commerce. The original letter stated, "To whom it may concern, we have recently heard that there are proposals to increase the fees for submarine telegraphs and wireless telegraphs, and that this issue of increasing fees will be brought up for discussion at the International Telegraph Conference to be held in Madrid, the capital of Spain, around September 10th. Our Chamber believes that commerce is currently difficult, and the price of national currency is unusually low, which results in the cost of sending a foreign telegram being several times higher. Our Chamber deeply felt this pain throughout the past year. From this, it can be inferred that merchants are suffering from the high cost of telegraph fees, which is self-evident. According to the purpose of the Telegraph Office's business, it is to guide merchants to increase the ratio of telegrams sent in order to expand their business. Therefore, it is better to have small profits and large sales than to increase fees and make people retreat. At the current fee rate, telegraphers already feel that telegraph fees are expensive. Once the price is increased, the consequences are imaginable. This matter is inherently detrimental to commerce, and it seems that it would also reduce the business of the Telegraph Office. Moreover, the Telegraph Office should also have the responsibility of considering the public welfare, and it does not seem appropriate to only focus on increasing revenue. We should request your office to maintain the status quo and exempt Shanghai people from the burden of increased telegraph fees. That would be the most desirable."

Yesterday's Board Meeting of the Chapei Epidemic Hospital 129

Endorsed Reorganization into a Contagious Disease Hospital

The Chapei Epidemic Hospital, initiated by Wu Xingya, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, and others, has been benefiting the poor since its establishment, earning a great reputation. The hospital convened its first board meeting on the 9th of this month at the Atlantic European Restaurant on Foochow Road. Eleven members attended, including Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Pan Gongzhan, Wen Zongyao, Zou Runqing, Du Yuesheng, Wang Yansong, Gu Xinyi, Wang Bin'yan, Zhu Yaxiong, and Zhang Binghui. Other board members, such as Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Xiaolin, Lin Kanghou, Yang Xiaotian, Chen Renhe, and He Yiming, were absent due to other commitments. Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs Wu Xingya was temporarily ill and also absent. After the meeting proceeded as scheduled, Director Yu Qiaqing was elected as the temporary chairman. Zhang Binghui, a board member and director of affairs, then reported on the preparations for the hospital, stating that the hospital's opening expenses, including repairing buildings, purchasing medicines and equipment, etc., were handled frugally, and that no expense was excessive. The hired doctors were all experienced scholars who were serious and responsible for their medical duties. As a result, poor people came upon hearing of the hospital. In the month since opening, more than 700 patients have been treated, and more than 100 have been hospitalized. While we do not dare to boast of achievements, we can at least say we have done no wrong. However, the hospital is currently experiencing financial difficulties. During the preparatory period, Director Du Yuesheng advanced 5,000 yuan to cover the opening expenses. Now, little remains. We hope that all directors will enthusiastically maintain the hospital and work hard to raise funds in order to make progress. Next, Zhu Yaxiong, a board member and director of medical affairs, reported on the medical aspects of the hospital. Then, discussion began. The chairman reported that the proposal by Directors Zhu and Zhang to reorganize the hospital into a contagious disease hospital was more important, and requested that all directors express their opinions. After joint discussion, it was decided that Directors Zhu and Zhang would continue to actively prepare, and Zhang would also be responsible for negotiating a permanent cooperation agreement with the person in charge of the Guangdong Hospital. It was also decided that another meeting would be held at the end of this month to make further decisions, and the meeting was adjourned.

Lawyers Association's Criminal Code Revision Committee 130

The Criminal Code Revision Committee of the Republic of China Lawyers Association convened its fifth committee meeting yesterday at 2:00 PM. Attendees included Shan Yuhua, Zhang Tao, Liu Liumin, Li Shirui, Hu Zhen, Yu Zhongluo, Guo Wei, Shen Junru, and Zhao Chen. Li Shirui was elected as chairman, and Dai Jixian recorded the minutes. The proposals are listed below: (1) The chairman reported the meeting minutes of the Shanghai committee members from the previous meeting, and submitted the previous meeting's proposals on revising the criminal law for discussion and approval item by item. (1) Regarding the proposal to unify the criminal law code, (passed by resolution). (2) Regarding the criminal procedure law proposal, (1) the proposal to unify the judicial organs (resolved, passed). (2) The proposal to abolish the procuratorate system and adopt prosecution by the victim as the principle and prosecution by the state as the exception (resolved) passed. (3) The proposal to adopt a lawyer interrogation system (resolved) passed. (4) The proposal to adopt a compromise jury system (resolved) passed. (5) The proposal to adopt a state compensation system for wrongful convictions (resolved) passed. (6) The proposal to restore the Dengwen Drum system (resolved) passed. (7) The proposal to restrict the detention of defendants (resolved) passed. For the above seven items, in addition to the already appointed Yu Zhongluo as drafter, Li Shirui and Lin Dawen were also appointed, with a time limit of three months. (3) Regarding the content of the criminal law revision, including (1) changing the names of crimes, (2) adopting security measures, (3) stipulating the crime of usury and exploitation, (4) stipulating the crime of insulting the state, (5) stipulating the crime of obstructing legitimate patriotic movements, (6) stipulating the crime of losing national territory, (7) the crime of losing national rights, and (8) the proposal that those who offer bribes and confess be innocent, were submitted for discussion (resolved) except for item 5, the crime of obstructing legitimate patriotic movements, which should be cancelled, all other proposals were passed. For the above content of the criminal law revision, in addition to the originally appointed Guo Wei and Zhao Chen, Shan Yuhua, Li Shirui, and Qiu Fenling were also appointed, and Zhao Chen was appointed as the chairman of the committee. In case of difficulties, meetings will be convened at any time. (4) The proposals of the day will be sent to all committee members and appointed members for review. After the discussion, the meeting was adjourned.

Reaction to the 30th Telegram of the People's Movement Committee 131

Since the People's Movement Committee of the Central Party Headquarters issued the "Nurturing Telegram," it has aroused repercussions from industrial groups and domestic goods factories across the country. They have jointly issued a declaration, the details of which were recorded in previous reports. On the 30th of last month, the People's Movement Committee issued another "30th Telegram," which extended the meaning of the "Nurturing Telegram." Now, major factories have jointly issued a declaration. At the same time, the China National Products Maintenance Association, the Citizens' Association for Promoting National Products, the Shanghai National Products Factory Federation, the Nanking Road Business Federation, the Shanghai Machine-made National Products Factory Federation, and the First District Branch of the Citizens' Association (six groups), telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters to request clarification. The China General Federation of Industry also telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters, the Central Political Conference, and the National Government separately, requesting correction. The original text has been found and is copied below:

Declaration of Various Factories Regarding the "Nurturing Telegram" of the People's Movement Committee and the request for the Municipal Party Committee and the Municipal Government to use extraordinary measures to force the start of work, we have previously expressed our opinions in the newspapers. After reading the newspaper, we learned that the People's Movement Committee had another "30th" telegram to Mayor Wu, stating that our declaration was a public criticism and disregard for the law, which deeply confused us. We believe that even if a court precedent is appropriate, scholars are still allowed to publicly comment after the judgment. Therefore, regarding the compliance of the People's Movement Committee's "Nurturing Telegram" with laws and regulations, we, who have a personal stake, hold a skeptical attitude and seek a fair answer, which is the same nature as criticizing precedents. We did not expect to be accused of disrespecting dignity and disregarding the law for this reason. This is something we did not anticipate and still do not understand. The "30th" telegram stated that the case has been investigated by the Municipal Government and should be resolved according to law. Therefore, the "Nurturing Telegram" advocating for extraordinary measures to force the start of work is in absolute opposition to resolving the issue according to law. If resolving the issue according to law is correct, then forcing the start of work is wrong. The People's Movement Committee stated that based on the workers' appeal to the committee, several months have passed, the situation has become more serious, and the requests of the factory owners cannot be the only consideration, ignoring the workers. Therefore, the only way to resolve this case is to urge the Municipal Government to quickly arbitrate according to the parties' requests. The reason why the "Nurturing Telegram" aroused criticism is the point of using extraordinary measures to force the start of work. If the government abandons its legal arbitration procedures and resorts to extraordinary measures, then both the employers and employees can abandon their legal procedures for requesting arbitration and each resort to their own extraordinary measures to seek victory. This would only increase the severity of the situation, not bring happiness to the people. We protect the Party and the country, protect order, and must protect the rule of law. Therefore, we have always been willing to offer sincere words as humble suggestions to the People's Movement Committee. If extraordinary measures are deemed necessary to achieve the goal of assisting workers, it is equivalent to the country establishing procedures for arbitration and all the usual means based on laws and regulations, exclusively to protect absolute private rights. Isn't the misunderstanding even worse? In short, to seek harmony between labor and capital, the rule of law must be respected first. To respect the rule of law, all extraordinary measures used outside the law must be rejected. Our so-called freedom of business refers to not being subject to extra-legal restrictions. As for monopoly business and prohibition of business, the laws have clear regulations, so there is no so-called extra-legal restriction, and it does not match the situation of Sanyou. The "30th" telegram used it as an analogy. Our simple minds cannot comprehend the deep meaning. As the saying goes, "The wind blows, and the grass bends." It also says, "The law is implemented from above." The organization leading the people must first respect the rule of law, so that the law does not become a mere formality. This is what we sincerely hope for. Please consider it carefully. [List of 60 factories]

Six Groups' Telegram to the Central Party Headquarters (Gray Telegram) To the Central Executive Committee in Nanjing, Greetings. The People's Movement Committee under your jurisdiction, in its 30th Telegram to Shanghai Mayor Wu, still insisted on using extraordinary measures to force employers to start work by a deadline in the Sanyou Industrial Company's labor-capital dispute, and stated that these manufacturers cited the Provisional Constitution to seek freedom of business, calling it a false pretext against the revolution, making the people reading it shudder. The Regulations on the Exercise of Governing Power, publicly announced on July 10, 1929, clearly state that the people's life, property, and freedom of body are protected by law and shall not be deprived without due process. Those illegally deprived are considered to have exceeded their authority. Is forcing employers to start work a deprivation of the people's freedom of property? The People's Movement Committee recommended it, is it without due process? Mayor Wu implemented extraordinary measures, did it exceed his authority? Once these are examined in detail, the correct answer can be found. Then, can the Regulations on the Exercise of Governing Power still be called law? Extraordinary is the opposite of ordinary. This only occurs when martial law is declared, and ordinary laws are suspended. Has Shanghai reached that state today? Since ancient times, when politics have been chaotic and laws have been disregarded, the people have often not followed the government's orders, but rather followed their own will. The government's control over the people has thus fallen into the path of "If one is not upright, even orders will not be followed." This kind of political phenomenon has long become an iron law that no country can avoid. Judging from this case, the extraordinary coercion, deprivation, and exceeding authority are all evident. However, from the Provisional Constitution to the above-mentioned Regulations, as well as various single laws on labor and labor-capital relations, all are laws. Applying them to resolve this case is more than sufficient. Now, instead of guiding the people to follow the law, they are replaced by extraordinary means, causing chaos. (Omission) Is this the will of Sun Yat-sen? (Omission) Speaking frankly, the suffering of the workers has reached its extreme. People are not made of wood or stone, how can we not sympathize? However, rescuing people from a well may result in the rescuer being drowned as well. Trying to help seedlings grow by pulling them up will ultimately lead to failure. The government, in charge of protective administration, also has its appropriate scope. Going beyond this, it becomes awkward. Your esteemed committee, as the central authority, coordinates the overall situation. In addition to the above questions, we respectfully request clarification on how to balance law and reality and reconcile labor and capital. The associations will respectfully comply with all instructions. We await your orders with utmost anxiety and anticipation. China National Products Maintenance Association, Citizens' Association for Promoting National Products, Shanghai National Products Factory Federation, Shanghai Machine-made National Products Factory Federation, Nanking Road Business Federation, First District Branch of the Citizens' Association, collectively.

The China General Federation of Industry's Telegram To the Central Party Headquarters, the Central Political Conference, and the National Government, Greetings. Previously, we read in the newspapers that regarding the labor-capital dispute at the Shanghai Sanyou Industrial Company, the People's Movement Guidance Committee of the Central Party Headquarters sent a "Nurturing Telegram" to the Shanghai Municipal Party Committee and the Municipal Government, requesting that they use extraordinary measures to force the start of work. Our association, based on the freedom of business stated in the Provisional Constitution, previously telegraphed the situation. At the same time, we requested that the highest Party and government authorities consider and explain the matter. While we were waiting for instructions, the People's Movement Committee issued another "30th Telegram," which, in addition to extending the meaning of the "Nurturing Telegram," also stated: (1) According to the highest principle of the People's Livelihood, the Provisional Constitution is not designed to protect absolute private rights. (2) Although business can be free, such as state monopoly business and prohibited business, it is not free. (3) There is no other country with the Three Principles of the People in the world, so there is no precedent for assisting workers. (4) The Party of the Three Principles of the People has the courage to create unprecedented examples in the world. We in the industrial business are inexperienced and have limited knowledge. We certainly do not understand the true meaning of the Party's principles as clearly as the People's Movement Guidance Organization. However, referring to the laws and regulations promulgated by the Central Government in the past, as well as the grand words and honest opinions expressed by the wise men of the Party and the country, found in various public and private documents and publications, their spirit and purpose generally do not match the points advocated by the "Nurturing Telegram" and the "30th Telegram." We deeply feel that, in the highest position of leading the people, at a time when labor-capital relations in China have not yet been harmonized, if one suddenly wants to establish a new path outside the scope of the law, then there is concern that the existing laws will lose their effectiveness, and the future facts will become more and more chaotic, complex, and difficult to handle. Considering the situation, this kind of extraordinary step does not seem to be tolerated by the current national society's emphasis on the rule of law. It is also a point that should be corrected urgently from the Party's standpoint. Investigating the highest principle of the People's Livelihood of the Three Principles of the People, the purpose is not only to seek welfare for all the people, but also to take into account the people's economic private rights. The Provisional Constitution, in this spirit, specifically established Article 37 to protect them. Outside the provisions of the article, only business that violates the law may have its operation stopped by law, and there is no provision for under what circumstances the law can force its operation. Furthermore, the Regulations on the Exercise of Governing Power promulgated by the Central Government in July 1929 state that the people's life and property are protected by law and shall not be deprived without due process. Illegal deprivation is considered exceeding authority. From these two points of view, the Provisional Constitution and the Regulations on the Exercise of Governing Power have not abandoned the protection of the people's private rights and the freedom to operate or cease operations. Under today's rule of law in China, it is still preserved as a right granted to the people by law and cannot be equated with state monopoly business and prohibited business, which have different natures. Respectfully reading the "30th Telegram," it says that there is no other country in the world with the Three Principles of the People, only China has it; there is no precedent in the world for assisting workers, and it relies on China to create it. However, we have occasionally glanced at foreign records regarding the assistance of workers. Internationally, there is the International Labor Bureau; in various national governments, there are labor departments to handle national labor administrative matters. Other matters, such as labor training, insurance, and savings, also have special agencies to handle them, which have become the focus of social undertakings. The precedents and old chapters seem to have existed for a long time. If it is said that extraordinary measures must be used to force the start of work and that this is considered the only policy to assist workers, we do not dare to think so. In short, we understand that, according to the highest principle of the People's Sovereignty, the government is the organization of the people, not the organization of the government. Today, the country has created a fundamental law with the aim of promoting politics and the people to get on the right track. On the one hand, it allows political forces to leave the standpoint of the law and use facts and emotions to resolve the law. The contradiction between them cannot help but make the general public doubt. In order to maintain the country's laws, we dare to speak frankly in order to prepare for the consideration of the Party and the country. China General Federation of Industry.

The Ta Kung She reports that the municipal government submitted the labor dispute at the Sanyou Industrial Company's Xiangyin Road factory to arbitration on the 31st of last month. The Cotton Textile Industry Union of the Seventh District yesterday presented a petition to Mayor Wu, which stated: "The petition is for the employer's deliberate excuse to appeal and stop paying for food expenses, and we request emergency sanctions. We believe that this case has been in dispute for eight months. On the 31st of last month, your government organized an arbitration committee and announced the arbitration, but the employer broke his promise and refused to accept the arbitration. As a result, the workers' clothes and belongings have been pawned. As the weather is getting colder, they have no way to keep warm. On the 7th of this month, it was time to receive food expenses. Representatives Xia Zhongzhao and Gong Zishen were sent to the company with Zhu Guilin, a representative of the Bureau of Social Affairs, to collect the expenses. The managing director Wang Xianhua met with them and said that he would have to ask the board of directors before paying. He said that he would probably not stop paying and asked them to come back on Friday to negotiate. When they went again with Chen Heqing, a representative of the Bureau of Social Affairs, Wang Xianhua still met them and said that he would definitely pay the full amount before 11:00 AM the next day. When they went again the next day, Wang Xianhua suddenly said that food expenses had also been stopped and no one was responsible, so they still did not receive it. It is found that the employer deliberately delayed and used every means. Recently, they have become even more aggravated and stopped providing food expenses, which not only caused the union's thousands of workers to suffer cruelly, but also put the Central People's Movement Committee's 'Nurturing Telegram,' the Ministry of Industry's 'Yang Telegram,' and your government's No. 142 approval in what position? Now, this case has no end in sight, and food expenses have been stopped again. Alas, the lives of the workers are not worth pity, but I am afraid that the government's credibility will be swept away. Therefore, we have specially prepared a document to petition your government to quickly take emergency measures to value the lives of the people, which is both a public virtue and a convenience. Respectfully presented to Wu, the Mayor of Shanghai, by the Cotton Textile Industry Union of the Seventh District of Shanghai."

Guowen News Agency reports: The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the Director-General of the Public Works Department of the Shanghai International Settlement yesterday, stating: "We are writing to inform you that according to a letter from lawyer Gu Xianzhang, he received a bill from the Shanghai Telephone Company and this morning received a letter from the company ordering him to pay the telephone bill from March 27 to September 30 of this year, amounting to thirty-three taels, three mace, and seven candareens of silver, in full by September 12, otherwise his telephone service will be suspended. We have learned that the company's price increase announcement was only disclosed in the newspapers on July 1. Now, in its letter, the company is demanding payment of telephone fees dating back to March 27. This type of price increase procedure violates the legal principle of 'no retroactivity.' Moreover, the contract signed between the Public Works Department and the company stipulated that after the telephone is converted to automatic operation, good service should be provided to the public, and special consideration would be given. Our telephone often experiences interruptions and dial tone problems, making it impossible to make calls in a timely manner. It often takes half an hour to contact the repair and inquiry departments of the company to request assistance, but even then, it is not possible to speak immediately. Can this type of service be called 'good'? This is not something the company can unilaterally decide. Unless all parties are brought together for a fair judgment, how can things be done fairly? We have reported these circumstances to the association. Inquiries regarding telephone price increases and incomplete service have been repeatedly submitted to your department for reconsideration. The situation described in the letter further proves the incompleteness of the service. We are writing to request that your department promptly handle the case jointly to avoid disputes."

Page 20

Appeal Judgment in the Zhicheng Gold Shop vs. Tian Xiangzhen Case 141

Tian Ordered to Repay Over Six Thousand Nine Hundred Taels

Feng Chaolun, the owner of Zhicheng Gold Shop, needed to buy and sell spot gold on behalf of customers but did not have the qualifications of a broker. Therefore, he affiliated his business name with brokers inside the Gold Exchange, such as Tongyurun, Yuanchun, Hengyu, and Jufengrun, i.e., the so-called "small colleagues." Acting as agents of these brokers, he bought and sold on behalf of customers. In the spring of last year, through the introductions of Wang Yiren, Tao Shutang, and others, Tian Xiangzhen began doing business with Zhicheng. He successively entrusted them to conduct spot gold transactions, establishing account names such as Ruji, Hengji, Zhenji, and Yingji. Profits and losses were settled monthly. By August of the autumn, after deducting the deposit, he owed six thousand nine hundred taels, nine mace, one candareen, and two cash of silver. Feng repeatedly demanded payment, but Tian ignored him and refused to pay. Feng then sued him in the First Special District Local Court. Tian, however, used the excuse that Zhicheng was not a broker, fabricating sophistry, saying that transactions in the exchange must be done by a broker to be legal. The Exchange Law does not allow buying and selling under the name of an affiliated broker. Even if there were transactions, they would be over-the-counter transactions, so the owed losses are naturally invalid. The judge in the first instance seemed to not understand the situation of the exchange and did not conduct a detailed investigation, thus being deceived. He then ruled against the plaintiff. Feng refused to accept the judgment and immediately hired lawyer Shen Yuesheng to represent him and filed an appeal with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. He clearly stated the facts of the case and the customs of the exchange in the appeal, requesting that the original judgment be overturned, that the owed amount be repaid according to the debt, and that the costs of both instances be borne. Moreover, since the appellant Tian Xiangzhen has now fled, fearing that he would not be able to compensate if the judgment is determined before execution, he specifically requested permission to declare provisional execution to protect his interests. Hu Min, the presiding judge of the Second Branch of the High Court, along with judges Ye Zai and Cai Zhaoying, held a hearing, summoning witnesses and documentary evidence. After careful examination, they recognized that the various documents submitted by Feng Chaolun were consistent after verification and without flaws, so Tian Xiangzhen's empty denial could not be allowed. They then changed the original judgment, ordering Tian Xiangzhen to repay Feng Chaolun six thousand nine hundred taels, nine mace, one candareen, and two cash of silver, plus interest at an annual rate of five percent from September 16, 20th year, until the end of execution. The litigation costs of the first and second instances were to be borne by Tian Xiangzhen. This judgment should be provisionally executed. Yesterday, the court ordered officials to deliver the judgment to the lawyers of both parties and informed them that if they did not accept the judgment, they could appeal to the Supreme Court within the statutory period.

Continued Trial of the Huade Road Murder Case 142

Defendant Claims It Was Not Intentional Homicide

He and the Deceased Were Friends for Four Years

Chen Yun (also known as Ke Ming), a 33-year-old Shaoxing native residing in the pavilion upstairs at No. 7 Chengxin Fang, Huade Road, allegedly used a kitchen knife to wound his friend Wang Zixi (i.e., Huang Zixi), a 23-year-old Pudong native, in the head and arms at around 5 a.m. on the 7th of this month. Wang died at Tongren Hospital at around 9 a.m. The prosecutor dispatched by the First Special District Court to the Philomene Road morgue to examine the body. The deceased became friends with him because he bought peaches. At that time, the defendant was honest and trustworthy and had the deceased's trust. The deceased had several bungalows in Xiaonanmen. Because the defendant was financially struggling and could not pay the rent, he allowed him to live there rent-free. Later, he heard that the defendant had embezzled dozens of yuan of rent for his own use. He does not know what his father and son talked about. After the incident, he went to the hospital to visit, but the deceased could not speak. He went to check and saw that the window of the pavilion upstairs was open, and the deceased was covered in blood and about to jump down. The defendant escaped through the front door, but was unable to escape because the iron gate at the entrance of the alley was closed. He heard it again a minute later. He quickly got up and went outside, seeing the deceased standing at the window, about to jump but stopping. He immediately said, "Don't worry, I'll come to save you," and broke through the back door. The defendant escaped from the front door. He went straight up to the pavilion upstairs. The deceased said, "Save me quickly," and he helped him to lie down on a desk near the window, seeing that his head and arms were injured and covered in blood. He was wearing a short shirt and pants but was barefoot. There was a bedding on the desk, and there were books on the desk. There was also a canvas bed in the drawer, stained with blood. There were also blood stains on the floor. He did not have time to ask him what happened and immediately called the fire brigade to go to Tongren Hospital. Detective Chen Baozhong testified that after the incident, he and Western Detective No. 309 went to the hospital to investigate. The deceased said that he was a partner at the Huayang Beef Company at No. 980 Baochang Road and had known the defendant for many years. He is a formal member of the Communist Party. After saying that, he stopped speaking. Yong Ren Yan Fuchang testified that his mother is the second landlord of the house, but his elderly and frail mother did not appear in court today. The defendant moved in alone, without a wife. He has never seen the deceased come before. He works in a certain place on Guling Road and does not sleep at home at night. When questioned, the defendant claimed that the desk was his, and the Communist books belonged to someone else. He did not pay attention. The defendant remained steadfast, so he ordered him to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing.

Conditions of the South City Wharf Renovation 144

Dredging and Repair of Floating Wharves Have Been Completed Long Ago

Embankment Project Can Be Completed Around October

It Can Rival the International Settlement in a Few Years

The wharves in the Sixteen Puli area of ​​Nanshi in this city were originally operated by merchants. The municipal authorities only collected taxes from the merchants and never intervened, resulting in many malpractices. Since the establishment of the municipal government, it ordered the Port Authority to take back the wharves with compensation and renovate them, and set up a wharf management office. At the end of the 19th year, the Port Authority was abolished, and the Public Utilities Bureau took over. The bureau believed that the wharves and warehouses were related, so it reorganized the wharf warehouse management office and separately appointed Xu Yuanfang, secretary of the bureau, as director, and Gao Shuan as deputy director. Since the bureau took over, it has strived to economize on office expenses and expand business expenses. Therefore, in less than two years, the wharf buildings have been completely renovated, and the management is also well-organized. Even in the current situation, it is more complete than the French Concession. In a few years, it can rival the International Settlement. The reporter paid a special visit to Director Huang Boqiao of the bureau yesterday to inquire about the bureau's operation of the wharves in the Nanshi area and the situation before the takeover. He was informed in detail and sent Director Xu Yuanfang and Deputy Director Gao Shuan to accompany him to visit the wharves in the Nanshi area. The details are recorded below.

Huang's Remarks: The Shanghai Nanshi steamboat wharves were originally operated by merchants (Dada Steamboat Company and Datong Shipping Company), so there are still Dada Wharf and Datong Wharf to this day. Later, various shipping companies believed that the Dada and other companies monopolized and controlled the wharves, affecting the shipping industry, and appealed to the municipal government. Therefore, in the 19th year, the municipal government ordered the competent Port Authority to take back the wharves with compensation and renovate them, and set up a wharf management office to be responsible for the work. At the end of the 19th year, the Port Authority was abolished and closed. The municipal government believed that the wharf part belonged to the scope of public utilities, so it was assigned to the bureau for continued operation in accordance with the municipal organization law. The bureau believed that the wharves and warehouses were related, and the warehouses had the function of assisting the development of the wharves, so it planned to operate the warehouses concurrently and changed the wharf management office to the wharf warehouse management office. When the bureau took over the Shanghai Nanshi wharves, the embankments were collapsed, the wharves were dilapidated, and the situation was so bad that it was almost unbearable. What made the shipping companies feel particularly difficult was that the water depth of each wharf was only one or two meters or so, and most of the ships could not dock. The order of the wharves was also chaotic, with vendors crowded, passengers and goods almost impossible to pass, and gangsters rampant, extorting money as commonplace. The bureau believes that under this situation, it is impossible to realize the municipal government's renovation proposal without thoroughly renovating and reforming. Therefore, on the one hand, it disbanded the original patrol team and established a wharf police station jointly with the Public Security Bureau, which was jointly commanded by the First District General Office and the wharf warehouse management office. It spared no effort to eliminate vendors and gangsters, and did everything possible to relieve the suffering of shipping companies and travelers. On the other hand, it applied to the municipal government for temporary funds to carry out dredging, repair of floating wharves, and embankment projects. The former two have been completed long ago, and the latter can also be completed around mid-October, with a total cost of no less than 300,000 yuan. It is making every effort to expand, in addition to the original wharves No. 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 10, 14, 15, and 16, wharves such as No. 9, 11, 12, 13, and 17 are also being planned for addition, and Wharf No. 9 is currently being built by the leased Lianan Shipping Bureau with垫欵, which is expected to be completed around Double Ten Festival. The bureau's only purpose in operating the wharves is to make it convenient for ships to dock, safe for passengers to get on and off, arouse the interest of Chinese people in traveling, and assist the development of the shipping industry. As for the management policy, it strives to economize on office expenses and fully expand business expenses. Therefore, although the current expenses have been repeatedly reduced due to the financial difficulties of the municipal treasury, it can still increase all equipment related to the safety of travelers, such as wharf lights, lifebuoys, and iron gates. If the municipal government can allow the wharf funds to be independent and operate completely according to the nature of the business, then the future development will be faster and more certain.

From Dongmen Road to Lujiabang, there are 17 wharves. From No. 1 to No. 8, they have been completely renovated. The other wharves are also being repaired and painted. All wharf building materials include two types: steel plates and foreign pine. The embankments are all built of stone blocks and have cement railings. From Dongmen Road to Guanqiao, the wharves are cleaned twice a day, so they are very clean. There are also designated places for loading and unloading goods to avoid hindering traffic. Vendors are absolutely not allowed to set up stalls on the wharves, but they are allowed to trade on the ships. Trucks transporting goods and passengers are only allowed to park in the open space on Dongmen Road and are not allowed to enter, so the order is extremely tidy. The coolies carrying goods on the wharves are all required to wear numbered clothing, otherwise they are not allowed to carry goods for customers. Therefore, there are very few cases of passengers losing their luggage. Recently, the warehouses in the Sixteen Puli area have generally felt that there is no place to stack goods, which is enough to show that general merchants are willing to load and unload goods in Nanshi. Therefore, the wharves in the Nanshi area can directly guarantee the safety of passengers after being renovated, and indirectly increase the prosperity of the steamboat business.

Coal Shop Manager Accused of Fraudulently Selling Goods Privately 145

Ge Jihua, the general manager of Zhongyuan Yiji Coal Shop at No. 42 Rongyang Lane, Pingwang Street, International Settlement, reported to the French Patrol the other day that the manager Huo Rongbo fraudulently used the name of Mingji Coal Shop to defraud Zhongyuan Coal Shop of more than 400 tons of Boshan coal and sold it privately to Tongyi and Guangtaishun silk factories. He then hid in the Anna Kim Road area under his jurisdiction, requesting an investigation. After receiving the report, the patrol head immediately ordered Detective Liu Jinrong to arrest Huo at his residence at No. 196 Anna Kim Road. Huo was arrested and sent to the Second Special Court yesterday, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo presided over the second criminal court for interrogation. First, Patrol Lawyer Fei Xizhen stated the case, saying that the defendant violated Article 363 of the Criminal Law, committing crimes such as fraud, embezzlement, and breach of trust. The defendant defrauded more than 400 tons of coal between August 1st and 10th, and requested an investigation according to law. Then, the plaintiff Ge Jihua stated that the defendant was previously the manager of Zhongyuan Coal Shop and sold the bills of lading for more than 3,000 tons of Boshan coal from the Hanyang Coal Depot to Mingji Coal Shop for a total of 33,700 yuan. A contract was signed, with one payment in advance and the remainder to be paid within one month. Unexpectedly, he could not collect the money when it was due, and Huo avoided meeting him. Therefore, he filed a lawsuit in the First Special Court, requesting compensation and requesting to detain the coal sold by Mingji to Tongyi and Baotaishun silk factories. Unexpectedly, the defendant Huo Rongbo suddenly came forward and issued a letter stating that the coal of Tongyi and Baotaishun factories was his personal property and all payments should be collected by him. He has a letter to prove that this Boshan coal was clearly sold by Zhongyuan Coal Shop to Mingji, and then resold by Mingji to Tongyi Baotaishun. The ownership of the goods still belongs to Zhongyuan Coal Shop, which clearly shows that the defendant has committed the crime of embezzlement, fraud, and breach of trust. He also hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to state everything and requested an incidental private lawsuit to recover the payment. Huo Rongbo confessed that the coal of Zhongyuan Coal Shop was actually sold to Mingji Coal Shop through the introduction of a merchant. Later, because they did not like the quality of the goods, they requested a deduction in price, so they stopped payment. As for the coal of Tongyi and Baotaishun factories, it was indeed the merchant's property. The reason is that the two factories had previously signed a one-year contract with Zhongyuan Coal Shop. During this period, all the coal used was supplied by Zhongyuan. Unexpectedly, in January of this year, Zhongyuan Coal Shop stopped supplying due to the impact of the war. Therefore, the two factory owners negotiated with me. In order to maintain the contract, the merchant purchased coal from Yicheng and several other coal shops in his personal name and supplied it to Tongyi and Baotaishun factories. There have been more than 1,000 tons so far, which can prove that Mingji is not a merchant's shop, let alone a shareholder. He requested a clear investigation. Then, witness Wang Qingwen testified that in August, the defendant used Mingji's name to sell Zhongyuan Boshan coal to Tongyi and Baotaishun factories, totaling more than 400 tons. After verifying the confession, Judge Zhang ordered the defendant to pay 5,000 yuan of silver and bail him out to await a further hearing on another date.

Mob Encircles Handcart 146

Questioning the Source and Destination of Serge Cloth

Sweet Soup Vendor's Child Cries Out in Distress

At 8 p.m. last night, near the south end of the Old Zha Gate Bridge, near the New Vegetable Market, a man resembling an old clerk from a business firm was pulling a handcart

loaded with more than a dozen pieces of serge cloth. When the nearby residents saw it, they immediately stepped forward to question the source of the goods and where they were being sent. The old clerk looked flustered and stammered. At this time, a young man dressed in a silk shirt next to him admitted that it was all his. Then, the audience began to condemn him, and disputes arose between them. Finally, the young man and the old clerk saw that the crowd was surging and difficult to resist, so they planned to break out of the encirclement and escape. At that time, a Chinese and Indian patrol happened to pass by and immediately telegraphed the Old Zha Gate Patrol Station, which sent Chinese and Western detectives to take all the people into the patrol station for interrogation. However, when the detectives arrived at the scene of the incident, all the onlookers scattered in a hubbub. A sweet soup vendor's stall parked outside the vegetable market was caught in the crossfire, causing all the bowls and dishes to be knocked over and smashed to pieces. The sweet soup was abandoned all over the ground. Although the child guarding the stall shouted and cried loudly, the panicked audience turned a deaf ear. As a result, the entire stall was destroyed, and the child had no way to complain, which was very pitiful.

New Building of the Municipal Ferry General Management Office Completed 149

Address: Daotang Street, Qingning Temple Road, Pudong

The Municipal Ferry General Management Office was originally located in Donggou, in the remaining houses of the former Shanghai Pudong Tanggong Relief Bureau. It has been there for many years. Now, with the expansion of the ferry business, the number of employees has increased tenfold compared to when it was taken over. The location of the office is narrow, and both work and hygiene are greatly affected. Moreover, the address is remote, and it is inconvenient to contact. Therefore, the office rented the temple property behind Daotang Street in Qingning Temple, the midpoint of the ferry route, to build the office of the General Management Office and employee housing. It has recently been completed and moved in. It is said that the building is a three-story building with a total of twenty-eight rooms up and down, only a hundred steps away from the Qingning Temple Wharf, which is very convenient.

Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Line Takes Over the Baoshan-Songhu-Yanghang Line 150

Direct Service to Wusong Pier

Connects with City-Operated Ferry

The long-distance bus service from Baoshan County to Wusong and Yanghang, which was suspended after being destroyed in the Songhu Incident, has been temporarily approved to be taken over by the Shanghai-Taicang long-distance bus company by the municipal authorities and the Baoshan County government. The service will resume today (September 11th). The Wusong route originally terminated at the train station. Now, to better connect land and water transportation, the route will be extended to the pier to connect with the city-operated Wusong ferry. This will allow people from Baoshan and other areas to take the city ferry from Wusong directly to the Shanghai Jinglu Bund, which is more convenient than taking land routes. The Wusong ferry schedule is as follows: (1) From Wusong: 9:30 AM, 11:30 AM, 1:30 PM, 3:30 PM, 5:30 PM; (2) From Shanghai: 7:00 AM, 9:00 AM, 11:00 AM, 1:00 PM, 3:00 PM. There are a total of ten round trips, all connecting with the long-distance buses.

Boy Scout Headquarters Approves the Postal Workers Boy Scout Troop 151

Listed as the 642nd Troop

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, recognizing that the Boy Scout movement in China only extends to a portion of schools and that very few social organizations have Boy Scout troops, felt it necessary to promote this. Therefore, in October of last year, upon the suggestion of Training Director Mr. Zhu Xuefan, the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union Boy Scout Troop was established in accordance with the Chinese Boy Scout Organization Regulations. The union appointed Mr. Lin Shaosen as troop leader, and Messrs. Wang Dingchang, Wu Chuliang, Shen Fu, and Shen Shenping as trainers. The troop consisted of over fifty members. At the beginning of its formation, the Songhu Incident occurred. The troop members, upholding their professional duty, braved all dangers and served in the war zone alongside the 19th Route Army Headquarters. A portion of the troop members were also assigned to work in military hospitals and refugee shelters, achieving considerable merit. It is reported that the troop has now been approved by the Chinese Boy Scout Headquarters and listed as the 642nd Troop of the Chinese Boy Scouts. The troop headquarters is located inside the Postal Workers' Union Club at 230 Laobazi Road.
